{{milestone:{label:6.5,id:UT22084-089-013-735}}}“However, noble one, the development of the first noble aspiration is like Sumeru; it is truly high because of all the roots of merit. Its cause is the perfection of generosity. 
{{milestone:{label:6.6,id:UT22084-089-013-736}}}“The second development of aspiration is like the earth in being the location of all activities in the Dharma. Its cause is the perfection of correct conduct. 
{{milestone:{label:6.7,id:UT22084-089-013-737}}}“The third development of aspiration is like the maned lion, the king of animals, because it has no terror, no anxiety, and no fear. Its cause is the perfection of patience. 
{{milestone:{label:6.8,id:UT22084-089-013-738}}}“The fourth development of aspiration is like the might, strength, force, diligence, and courage of Nārāyaṇa, because it is irreversible. Its cause is the perfection of diligence. 
{{milestone:{label:6.9,id:UT22084-089-013-739}}}“The fifth development of aspiration is like someone who is truly noble through their various good actions because they are never satisfied with their merit. Its cause is the perfection of meditation.
{{milestone:{label:6.10,id:UT22084-089-013-740}}}“The sixth development of aspiration is like the bright disk of the sun because it dispels deep darkness. Its cause is the perfection of wisdom. {{page:{number:78,id:UT22084-089-013-3029,folio:F.190.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.11,id:UT22084-089-013-741}}}“The seventh development of aspiration is like a head merchant who is wealthy with great treasure because it is a perfect adornment; it brings freedom from the wilderness of saṃsāra and fulfills all wishes. Its cause is the perfection of skill in methods.
{{milestone:{label:6.12,id:UT22084-089-013-742}}}“The eighth development of aspiration is like the pure disk of the full moon, because it completes purification from all obscurations. Its cause is the perfection of prayer. 
{{milestone:{label:6.13,id:UT22084-089-013-743}}}“The ninth development of aspiration is like the fulfillment of all wishes, because it is the domain of all the displays of the qualities of the pure buddha realms. Its cause is the perfection of strength.
{{milestone:{label:6.14,id:UT22084-089-013-744}}}“The tenth development of aspiration is like space because it has the way of the characteristics of a cakravartin due to having attained the consecration of mastery over all qualities, wisdom, and Dharmas. Its cause is the perfection of knowledge.
{{milestone:{label:6.15,id:UT22084-089-013-745}}}“Noble one, those are a bodhisattva’s ten developments of aspiration. Through having these one is called a bodhisattva, but ultimately, there is no enlightenment, there is no bodhisattva, and there is no aspiration of enlightenment.
{{milestone:{label:6.16,id:UT22084-089-013-746}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of generosity of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary of the power of faith; (2) the preliminary of contemplation; (3) the preliminary of superior aspiration; (4) the preliminary of the perfections; (5) the preliminary of great love; (6) the preliminary of great compassion; (7) the preliminary of being a support for beings; (8) the preliminary of the methods of gathering beings; (9) the preliminary of desiring the Dharma of the buddhas; and (10) the preliminary of wishing for omniscient wisdom. {{page:{number:79,id:UT22084-089-013-3030,folio:F.190.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.17,id:UT22084-089-013-747}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of generosity of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.18,id:UT22084-089-013-748}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of correct conduct of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary of pure physical conduct; (2) the preliminary of pure vocal conduct; (3) the preliminary of pure mental conduct; (4) the preliminary of nonviolence; (5) the preliminary of avoiding the lower existences; (6) the preliminary of avoiding the unfortunate states; (7) the preliminary of transcending the level of the śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas; (8) the preliminary of establishing the qualities of buddhahood; (9) the preliminary of complete aspiration; and (10) the preliminary of complete prayer.
{{milestone:{label:6.19,id:UT22084-089-013-749}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of correct conduct of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.20,id:UT22084-089-013-750}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of patience of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary of forsaking desire; (2) the preliminary of forsaking anger; (3) the preliminary of having no concern for one’s body; (4) the preliminary of not being concerned with one’s life; (5) the preliminary of aspiration; (6) the preliminary of ripening beings; (7) the preliminary of the strength of love; (8) the preliminary of patience for profound Dharma; (9) the preliminary of aspiration for that which is vast; and (10) the preliminary of dispelling ignorance.
{{milestone:{label:6.21,id:UT22084-089-013-751}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of patience of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.22,id:UT22084-089-013-752}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of diligence of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are {{page:{number:80,id:UT22084-089-013-3031,folio:F.191.a}}} (1) the preliminary that is thinking of what is to be done for all beings; (2) the preliminary that is rejoicing in the accomplishment of a virtuous body, speech, and mind; (3) the preliminary that is never being disheartened; (4) the preliminary that is the activity of attaining the level of irreversibility; (5) the preliminary that is correct effort; (6) the preliminary that is mindfulness; (7) the preliminary that is subjugating the enemy, which is the kleśas; (8) the preliminary that is being detached from all phenomena; (9) the preliminary that is the activity of ripening beings; and (10) the preliminary that is the accomplishment of omniscient knowledge.
{{milestone:{label:6.23,id:UT22084-089-013-753}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of diligence of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.24,id:UT22084-089-013-754}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of meditation of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary that is maintaining good qualities; (2) the preliminary that is samādhi; (3) the preliminary that is samāpatti; (4) the preliminary that is complete enlightenment; (5) the preliminary that is dhyāna and liberations; (6) the preliminary that is the faculty of samādhi; (7) the preliminary that is the strength of samādhi; (8) the preliminary that is forsaking the kleśas of all beings; (9) the preliminary that is completing the aggregation of samādhis; and (10) the preliminary that is guarding the Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:6.25,id:UT22084-089-013-755}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of meditation of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.26,id:UT22084-089-013-756}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of wisdom of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary that is being skilled in the skandhas; (2) the preliminary that is being skilled in the dhātus; (3) the preliminary that is being skilled in the āyatanas; (4) the preliminary that is being skilled in dependent origination; (5) the preliminary that is being skilled in the truths; {{page:{number:81,id:UT22084-089-013-3032,folio:F.191.b}}} (6) the preliminary that is dispelling all wrong views; (7) the preliminary that is the faculty of wisdom; (8) the preliminary that is patience toward the quality of birthlessness; (9) the preliminary that is completing all the qualities of buddhahood; and (10) the preliminary that is seeing unobscured wisdom.
{{milestone:{label:6.27,id:UT22084-089-013-757}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of wisdom of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.28,id:UT22084-089-013-758}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of the skill in methods of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary that is engaging with the motivations and conduct of beings; (2) the preliminary that is becoming a support for beings; (3) the preliminary that is great love and compassion; (4) the preliminary that is the ripening of beings; (5) the preliminary that is engagement in all the qualities of buddhahood; (6) the preliminary that is seeing special wisdom; (7) the preliminary that is the purification of the perfections; (8) the preliminary that is the contemplation of things exactly as they are; (9) the preliminary that is the accomplishment of the strength of the mind; and (10) the preliminary that is the attainment of the level of irreversibility.
{{milestone:{label:6.29,id:UT22084-089-013-759}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of skill in methods of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.30,id:UT22084-089-013-760}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of prayer of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the massed mental conduct of all beings; (2) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the massed kleśas of all beings; (3) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the massed faculties of all beings; (4) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the massed motivations and aspirations of all beings; {{page:{number:82,id:UT22084-089-013-3033,folio:F.192.a}}} (5) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the massed motivations, higher motivations, and aspirations of all beings; (6) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements in the separate world realms and the three realms; (7) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the massed motivations and propensities of all beings; (8) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the massed deaths and rebirths of all beings; (9) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the movements of the display of the three aggregations of all beings; and (10) the preliminary that is the knowledge of ripening beings who have untiring faculties.
{{milestone:{label:6.31,id:UT22084-089-013-761}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of prayer of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.32,id:UT22084-089-013-762}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of strength of a bodhisattva. What are the ten? They are (1) the preliminary that is the primordial nonorigination of all phenomena; (2) the preliminary that is the primordial nonexistence of the characteristics of all phenomena; (3) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the primordial birthlessness of all phenomena; (4) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the primordial nonexistence of all phenomena; (5) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the primordial nonformation of all phenomena; (6) the preliminary that is the knowledge that all phenomena do not enter; (7) the preliminary that is the knowledge that all phenomena do not turn back; (8) the preliminary that is the knowledge that all phenomena have the nature of nothingness; (9) the preliminary that is the knowledge that the beginning, middle, and end of all phenomena are the same; and (10) the preliminary that is the absence of concepts or thoughts engaging with the true nature of all phenomena.
{{milestone:{label:6.33,id:UT22084-089-013-763}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of strength of the bodhisattvas. 
{{milestone:{label:6.34,id:UT22084-089-013-764}}}“Noble one, there are ten qualities that are preliminaries to the perfection of knowledge of a bodhisattva. {{page:{number:83,id:UT22084-089-013-3034,folio:F.192.b}}} What are these ten? They are (1) the preliminary that is the analysis that differentiates all phenomena; (2) the preliminary that is the completion of all good qualities; (3) the preliminary that is an immeasurable gathering of the accumulation of enlightenment; (4) the preliminary that is possessing a vast accumulation of merit and wisdom; (5) the preliminary that is the realization of vast great compassion; (6) the preliminary that is the knowledge that all phenomena do not enter; (7) the preliminary that is the knowledge of the levels of categories of the world realms; (8) the preliminary that is comprehending the realms of beings and the conduct motivated by the kleśas; (9) the preliminary that is the mental activity of comprehending and following the range of activity of the tathāgatas; and (10) the preliminary that is the higher perception and complete knowledge of the ten strengths, the fearlessnesses, and the unique qualities of a buddha.
{{milestone:{label:6.35,id:UT22084-089-013-765}}}“Noble one, those are the ten qualities that are the preliminaries for the perfection of knowledge of the bodhisattvas.
{{milestone:{label:6.36,id:UT22084-089-013-766}}}“Noble one, what is the meaning of perfection? The fulfillment of special conduct: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of vast and profound wisdom: that is the meaning of perfection. The absence of attachment to the composite and noncomposite: that is the meaning of perfection. The correct realization of the faults of saṃsāra: that is the meaning of perfection. Comprehending unwise beings: that is the meaning of perfection. Teaching the treasure of the Dharma that knows no cessation: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of unobscured liberation: that is the meaning of perfection. Knowing the realms of beings: that is the meaning of perfection. The realization of the sameness of generosity: that is the meaning of perfection. {{page:{number:84,id:UT22084-089-013-3035,folio:F.193.a}}} The fulfillment of the sameness of correct conduct: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of the sameness of patience: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of the sameness of diligence: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of the sameness of meditation: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of skill in knowing the perfection of wisdom: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of special conduct: that is the meaning of perfection. Having perfect knowledge of all phenomena: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of patience toward the quality of birthlessness: that is the meaning of perfection. The attainment of the level of irreversibility: that is the meaning of perfection. The purification of a buddha realm: that is the meaning of perfection. Ripening completely all beings: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of the wisdom of buddhahood at a Bodhimaṇḍa: that is the meaning of perfection. The subjugation of all māras: that is the meaning of perfection. Liberating and manifesting the nonduality of saṃsāra and nirvāṇa: that is the meaning of perfection. Reaching the perfection of qualities: that is the meaning of perfection. The eradication of adversaries: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of the ten strengths, the fearlessnesses, and the eighteen unique qualities of a buddha: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of special conduct: that is the meaning of perfection. The fulfillment of all the qualities of buddhahood: that is the meaning of perfection. Complete enlightenment as the highest, most complete enlightenment: that is the meaning of perfection. Turning the wheel of the Dharma in twelve ways: that is the meaning of perfection. {{page:{number:85,id:UT22084-089-013-3036,folio:F.193.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.37,id:UT22084-089-013-768}}}“Noble one, the omen of the first bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing that the trichiliocosm world realm becomes filled with a hundred thousand quintillion treasures.
{{milestone:{label:6.38,id:UT22084-089-013-769}}}“The omen of the second bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing that the trichiliocosm world realm becomes like the palm of the hand and is perfectly adorned by many hundred thousand quintillions of jewels.
{{milestone:{label:6.39,id:UT22084-089-013-770}}}“The omen of the third bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing oneself as a warrior holding weapons, wearing strong armor, and subjugating one’s foes.
{{milestone:{label:6.40,id:UT22084-089-013-771}}}“The omen of the fourth bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing four circles of wind from the four directions scattering various flowers over the great circle of the all-possessing earth.
{{milestone:{label:6.41,id:UT22084-089-013-772}}}“The omen of the fifth bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing a woman adorned in every kind of jewelry placing a garland of magnolia flowers on one’s head.
{{milestone:{label:6.42,id:UT22084-089-013-773}}}“The omen of the sixth bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing a pool with four stairways, at the bottom of which is gold sand. The pool is filled with water that is not muddied, but clear, and it possesses the eight good qualities. Its water is adorned with blue lotuses, night lotuses, and white lotuses, and one uses it for one’s own pleasure.
{{milestone:{label:6.43,id:UT22084-089-013-774}}}“The omen of the seventh bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing the chasm of the hells to one’s right and left and returning from that unwounded and unharmed. {{page:{number:86,id:UT22084-089-013-3037,folio:F.194.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.44,id:UT22084-089-013-775}}}“The omen of the eighth bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing that one carries upon both shoulders lions, the kings of beasts, crowned with their manes, terrifying all the smaller beasts.
{{milestone:{label:6.45,id:UT22084-089-013-776}}}“The omen of the ninth bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing oneself as a cakravartin king encircled by many hundred thousand quintillions of people, as one is looking straight ahead with a white parasol adorned with various jewels held above one’s head.
{{milestone:{label:6.46,id:UT22084-089-013-777}}}“The omen of the tenth bodhisattva bhūmi of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is seeing the body of a tathāgata who is looking straight ahead and teaching the Dharma, and who is the color of gold with a fathom-wide aura, encircled by many hundred thousand quintillions of Brahmās.
{{milestone:{label:6.47,id:UT22084-089-013-778}}}“Noble one, those ten are the omens of the ten bodhisattva bhūmis of the bodhisattva mahāsattvas.
{{milestone:{label:6.48,id:UT22084-089-013-780}}}“Noble one, why is the first bhūmi called Perfect Joy? The first bhūmi is called Perfect Joy because at the beginning, a mind that transcends the world, which had not previously been attained, is made manifest, and as the aspiration to a great goal has been fulfilled, there is a great joy that arises.
{{milestone:{label:6.49,id:UT22084-089-013-781}}}“The second bhūmi is called Stainless because it is purified of even the slightest stains of downfalls and of all faults in conduct. 
{{milestone:{label:6.50,id:UT22084-089-013-782}}}“The third bhūmi is called Shining because there is the shining light of measureless wisdom and the wisdom of samādhi, which cannot be undermined, cannot be outshone by anything, and remains in the power of retention that holds what has been heard. 
{{milestone:{label:6.51,id:UT22084-089-013-783}}}“The fourth bhūmi is called Blazing because the fire of wisdom incinerates all kleśas, and the blazing light of meditation on the qualities of the aspects of enlightenment increases. {{page:{number:87,id:UT22084-089-013-3038,folio:F.194.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.52,id:UT22084-089-013-784}}}“The fifth bhūmi is called Difficult Training because the method of meditation and the supreme wisdom are difficult to master, and the kleśas that are difficult to subjugate through the paths of seeing and meditation have been subjugated.
{{milestone:{label:6.53,id:UT22084-089-013-785}}}“The sixth bhūmi is called Manifested because there is the manifestation of the absence of obstruction from composite phenomena, and the manifestation of all featureless mentation. 
{{milestone:{label:6.54,id:UT22084-089-013-786}}}“The seventh bhūmi is called Gone Far because there is a long, continuous meditation in liberated samādhi, because of there being no obstacles to stainless qualities and because of featureless mentation.
{{milestone:{label:6.55,id:UT22084-089-013-787}}}“The eighth bhūmi is called Unwavering because, through attainment of the mastery of featureless mentation, the kleśas are unable to cause instability.
{{milestone:{label:6.56,id:UT22084-089-013-788}}}“The ninth bhūmi is called Perfect Understanding because, through the mastery of teaching the Dharma in all its aspects, there are no transgressions and there is the attainment of unimpeded, vast understanding. 
{{milestone:{label:6.57,id:UT22084-089-013-789}}}“The tenth bhūmi is called Cloud of Dharma because the Dharma body is like the sky covered by the clouds of great wisdom.
{{milestone:{label:6.58,id:UT22084-089-013-790}}}“Noble one, the first bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of attachment to the features of phenomena and individuals, and the ignorance of being terrified by the torments of saṃsāra and the lower realms.
{{milestone:{label:6.59,id:UT22084-089-013-791}}}“The second bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of the delusion of subtle downfalls, and the ignorance that gives rise to various kinds of actions and conduct.
{{milestone:{label:6.60,id:UT22084-089-013-792}}}“The third bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of wishing to attain what has not been attained, and ignorance concerning attaining the supreme, sublime power of retention.
{{milestone:{label:6.61,id:UT22084-089-013-793}}}“The fourth bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of craving for the delight of resting in meditation, and the ignorance of craving for pure Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:6.62,id:UT22084-089-013-794}}}“The fifth bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of being saddened by saṃsāra, and the ignorance of exerting oneself for nirvāṇa. {{page:{number:88,id:UT22084-089-013-3039,folio:F.195.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.63,id:UT22084-089-013-795}}}“The sixth bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of perceiving the movement of the composite, and the ignorance of perceiving evident features.
{{milestone:{label:6.64,id:UT22084-089-013-796}}}“The seventh bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of manifest subtle features, and the ignorance of featureless mentation.
{{milestone:{label:6.65,id:UT22084-089-013-797}}}“The eighth bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of exertion toward featurelessness, and the ignorance of attaining power over the grasping of features.
{{milestone:{label:6.66,id:UT22084-089-013-798}}}“The ninth bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of not being skilled in whatever Dharma is taught as being limitless, with limitless words and letters, and the ignorance of not having attained the power of eloquence.
{{milestone:{label:6.67,id:UT22084-089-013-799}}}“The tenth bhūmi is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of not having attained the power of great higher cognitions, and the ignorance of not being skilled in subtle, secret meanings and actions. 
{{milestone:{label:6.68,id:UT22084-089-013-800}}}“The bhūmi of buddhahood is obscured by these two kinds of ignorance: the ignorance of the obscuration of knowledge and the ignorance of the negative propensities of extremely subtle kleśas.
{{milestone:{label:6.69,id:UT22084-089-013-801}}}“Noble one, the bodhisattva who is on the first bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of generosity.
{{milestone:{label:6.70,id:UT22084-089-013-802}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the second bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of correct conduct.
{{milestone:{label:6.71,id:UT22084-089-013-803}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the third bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of patience.
{{milestone:{label:6.72,id:UT22084-089-013-804}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the fourth bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of diligence.
{{milestone:{label:6.73,id:UT22084-089-013-805}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the fifth bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of meditation.
{{milestone:{label:6.74,id:UT22084-089-013-806}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the sixth bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of wisdom.
{{milestone:{label:6.75,id:UT22084-089-013-807}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the seventh bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of skill in methods.
{{milestone:{label:6.76,id:UT22084-089-013-808}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the eighth bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of prayer.
{{milestone:{label:6.77,id:UT22084-089-013-809}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the ninth bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of strength.
{{milestone:{label:6.78,id:UT22084-089-013-810}}}“The bodhisattva who is on the tenth bodhisattva bhūmi has ascended to the perfection of knowledge. {{page:{number:89,id:UT22084-089-013-3040,folio:F.195.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.79,id:UT22084-089-013-811}}}“Noble one, the first development of aspiration of a bodhisattva mahāsattva is obtained and arises through the samādhi that is a superior jewel. 
{{milestone:{label:6.80,id:UT22084-089-013-812}}}“The second development of aspiration is obtained and arises through the samādhi that has no location.
{{milestone:{label:6.81,id:UT22084-089-013-813}}}“The third development of aspiration is obtained and arises through samādhi that is unwavering.
{{milestone:{label:6.82,id:UT22084-089-013-814}}}“The fourth development of aspiration is obtained and arises through samādhi that is irreversible.
{{milestone:{label:6.83,id:UT22084-089-013-815}}}“The fifth development of aspiration is obtained and arises through the samādhi of precious flowers.
{{milestone:{label:6.84,id:UT22084-089-013-816}}}“The sixth development of aspiration is obtained and arises through the samādhi of the brilliance of sunlight.
{{milestone:{label:6.85,id:UT22084-089-013-817}}}“The seventh development of aspiration is obtained and arises through the samādhi that accomplishes all goals.
{{milestone:{label:6.86,id:UT22084-089-013-818}}}“The eighth development of aspiration is obtained and arises through the samādhi of the directly perceived presence of the present buddhas.
{{milestone:{label:6.87,id:UT22084-089-013-819}}}“The ninth development of aspiration is obtained and developed through the samādhi of the lamp of wisdom.
{{milestone:{label:6.88,id:UT22084-089-013-820}}}“The tenth development of aspiration is obtained and arises through the samādhi that is heroic.
{{milestone:{label:6.89,id:UT22084-089-013-821}}}“Noble one, on the first bodhisattva bhūmi of the bodhisattva mahāsattvas there arises and is obtained the dhāraṇī called consecration: 
{{milestone:{label:6.90,id:UT22084-089-013-822}}}tadyathā | pūrṇamno rathe duhu duhu duhu yāvat sūryāvabhāsatā yāvat candra daudatte dāvād arakṣamān daṇạparihāram kuru svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.91,id:UT22084-089-013-823}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in a Ganges River will protect the bodhisattvas on the first bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.92,id:UT22084-089-013-824}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all fears, which means freed from vicious beasts such as tigers and lions; {{page:{number:90,id:UT22084-089-013-3041,folio:F.196.a}}} freed from all pretas, humans, nonhumans, and so on; and freed from enemies, robbers, the planets, the kleśas, and the five kinds of obscurations, and they will remember the first bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.93,id:UT22084-089-013-825}}}“Noble one, on the second bodhisattva mahāsattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called invincibility arises and is obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.94,id:UT22084-089-013-826}}}tadyathā | uttoli ciriciri uttorā toranaṃ śānto śānto attoli hulu hulu svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.95,id:UT22084-089-013-827}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in two Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the second bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.96,id:UT22084-089-013-828}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors, which means freed from vicious beasts, vicious pretas, human and nonhuman attacks, opposing enemies, the planets, the kleśas, suffering, and the five kinds of obscurations, and they will remember the second bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.97,id:UT22084-089-013-829}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the third bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called firm presence will arise and be obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.98,id:UT22084-089-013-830}}}tadyathā | daṇṭhike vaṇṭhike karaṭhī kauraṭhi kaiyūre tantili svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.99,id:UT22084-089-013-831}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in three Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the third bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.100,id:UT22084-089-013-832}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—vicious beasts, vicious demons, attacks from humans and nonhumans and so on, the planets, opposing enemies, various kinds of suffering, and the five kinds of obscurations—and {{page:{number:91,id:UT22084-089-013-3042,folio:F.196.b}}} they will remember the third bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.101,id:UT22084-089-013-833}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the fourth bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called unsubjugated will arise and be obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.102,id:UT22084-089-013-834}}}tadyathā | śiriśiri dimi dimini dari darini śiri śiriṇi viśalā viśālā paśa paśani bandhniye svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.103,id:UT22084-089-013-835}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in four Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the fourth bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.104,id:UT22084-089-013-836}}}“Whoever possesses and recites this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—fierce beasts, malevolent pretas, humans and nonhumans and so on, opposing enemies, the torments of various kinds of suffering, the planets, and the five kinds of obscurations—and they will remember the fourth bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.105,id:UT22084-089-013-837}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the fifth bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called the array of various qualities will arise and be obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.106,id:UT22084-089-013-838}}}tadyathā | hari hariṇi ciri ciriṇi karimāṇi saṅkarimāṇi sambāsani jambhani stambhani mohani svamūkke svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.107,id:UT22084-089-013-839}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in five Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the fifth bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.108,id:UT22084-089-013-840}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—fierce beasts, malevolent pretas, humans and nonhumans and so on, opposing enemies, the torments of various kinds of suffering, the planets, and the five kinds of obscurations—and they will remember the fifth bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.109,id:UT22084-089-013-841}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the sixth bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called the lamp of the field of wisdom will arise and be obtained: {{page:{number:92,id:UT22084-089-013-3043,folio:F.197.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:6.110,id:UT22084-089-013-842}}}tadyathā | vitori vitori mariṇi kali kali vidho hanati lulu lulu culu culu toluva toluva śaśa śaccha variśa svasti sarva satvānāṃ siddhyantu mama mantravādāni svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.111,id:UT22084-089-013-843}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in six Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the sixth bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.112,id:UT22084-089-013-844}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—fierce beasts, malevolent pretas, humans and nonhumans and so on, opposing enemies, the torments of various kinds of suffering, the planets, and the five kinds of obscurations—and they will remember the sixth bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.113,id:UT22084-089-013-845}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the seventh bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called superiority will arise and be obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.114,id:UT22084-089-013-846}}}tadyathā | jaha jaharu jaha jaha jaharu vailuke amṛteghaṇe puruśaṇe vairutike varubatte vidhi hike vinda vilini amṛlutike bhaijuyu bhaijuyu svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.115,id:UT22084-089-013-847}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in seven Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the seventh bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.116,id:UT22084-089-013-848}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—fierce beasts, malevolent pretas, humans and nonhumans and so on, opposing enemies, the torments of various kinds of suffering, the planets, and the five kinds of obscurations—and they will remember the seventh bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.117,id:UT22084-089-013-849}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the eighth bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called unpolluted thought will arise and be obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.118,id:UT22084-089-013-850}}}tadyathā | sari {{page:{number:93,id:UT22084-089-013-3044,folio:F.197.b}}} śari śiriṇi mitemite kari kari heru heru curu curu bandhani svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.119,id:UT22084-089-013-851}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in eight Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the eighth bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.120,id:UT22084-089-013-852}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—fierce beasts, malevolent pretas, humans and nonhumans and so on, opposing enemies, the torments of various kinds of suffering, the planets, and the five kinds of obscurations—and they will remember the eighth bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.121,id:UT22084-089-013-853}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the ninth bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called infinite adornment will arise and be obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.122,id:UT22084-089-013-854}}}tadyathā | haricaṇḍalike kulamābhate toraśipata patasi śiri śiri gaśiri gaviśiri svasti sarvasatvānāṃ svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.123,id:UT22084-089-013-855}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in nine Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the ninth bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.124,id:UT22084-089-013-856}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—fierce beasts, malevolent pretas, humans and nonhumans and so on, opposing enemies, the torments of various kinds of suffering, the planets, and the five kinds of obscurations—and they will remember the ninth bhūmi.
{{milestone:{label:6.125,id:UT22084-089-013-857}}}“Noble one, for the bodhisattva mahāsattva who is on the tenth bodhisattva bhūmi, the dhāraṇī called the unceasing casket will arise and be obtained: 
{{milestone:{label:6.126,id:UT22084-089-013-858}}}tadyathā | siddhe susiddhe mocani mokṣani mukte vimukte amale vimale damale māṅgale hiraṇyagarbhe ratnagarbhe samantabhadre sarvārtha sādhana manasi mahāmanasi adbhute atyadbhute araje {{page:{number:94,id:UT22084-089-013-3045,folio:F.198.a}}} viraje ucyute amṛte araje viraje brahme brahma sārwpūraṇi pūraṇa manorathe svāhā |
{{milestone:{label:6.127,id:UT22084-089-013-859}}}“Noble one, this dhāraṇī is recited so that more buddha bhagavats than there are grains of sand in ten Ganges Rivers will protect the bodhisattvas on the tenth bhūmi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.128,id:UT22084-089-013-860}}}“Those who recite and possess this dhāraṇī mantra will be freed from all terrors—fierce beasts, malevolent pretas, humans and nonhumans and so on, opposing enemies, the torments of various kinds of suffering, the planets, and the five kinds of obscurations—and they will remember the tenth bhūmi.”
{{milestone:{label:6.129,id:UT22084-089-013-861}}}Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva by the name of Unobstructed Appearance of the Light of a Lion’s Ornament, having heard the Bhagavat teach those dhāraṇīs, rose from his seat and, with his upper robe over one shoulder, knelt on his right knee, placed his palms together in homage, bowed down to the Bhagavat’s two feet, and praised him with these verses:
{{milestone:{label:6.130,id:UT22084-089-013-862}}}“I praise you, who are beyond example,
The unique Bhagavat who liberates
Beings with weak knowledge
In the profound Dharma without characteristics.
{{milestone:{label:6.131,id:UT22084-089-013-863}}}“The Tathāgatas’ eyes of wisdom
Do not see a single characteristic of phenomena. 
Your eyes of the pure Dharma
Have complete, inconceivable clarity.
{{milestone:{label:6.132,id:UT22084-089-013-864}}}“Every phenomenon has no birth,
And neither does it cease.
Through seeing equally in that way,
One will be in the highest state.
{{milestone:{label:6.133,id:UT22084-089-013-865}}}“Not being terrified of saṃsāra,
Or remaining in nirvāṇa—
Not dwelling in the two extremes—
In that way nirvāṇa is attained.
{{milestone:{label:6.134,id:UT22084-089-013-866}}}“Because you make no distinction
Between that which is pure and impure,
The Bhagavat knows one taste {{page:{number:95,id:UT22084-089-013-3046,folio:F.198.b}}}
And has attained supreme purity.
{{milestone:{label:6.135,id:UT22084-089-013-867}}}“The immeasurable body of the Bhagavat
Does not teach even a single word,
And yet a rain of Dharma brings satisfaction
To the entire multitude of this assembly.
{{milestone:{label:6.136,id:UT22084-089-013-868}}}“Although he does not see the
Characteristics of all these beings,
The Bhagavat always protects them
From all kleśas and suffering.
{{milestone:{label:6.137,id:UT22084-089-013-869}}}“There is no happiness or suffering 
No permanence or impermanence,
Self or selflessness, and so on; no singleness
Or multiplicity; and no birth or cessation.
{{milestone:{label:6.138,id:UT22084-089-013-870}}}“He teaches and elucidates
That kind of meaning.
The buddhas know this meaning,
Which is like an empty echo.
{{milestone:{label:6.139,id:UT22084-089-013-871}}}“As the Dharma realm is indivisible,
There are no other contradictory yānas,
But he has made the division into three
In order to liberate beings.”
{{milestone:{label:6.140,id:UT22084-089-013-872}}}Then Maheśvara, the king of the Brahmā devas, rose from his seat and, with his upper robe over one shoulder, knelt on his right knee, placed his palms together in homage, bowed down to the Bhagavat’s two feet, and said to the Bhagavat, “This Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light, is very rare; it is beyond evaluation. It is good in the beginning, good in the middle, and good in the end; it has a good meaning; it has good words; it is unmixed and perfect; and it makes perfect all the Buddhadharma. Whoever possesses and holds it is someone who fulfills the deeds of the buddha bhagavats.”
{{milestone:{label:6.141,id:UT22084-089-013-873}}}“Noble one, it is as you have said,” replied the Bhagavat. “Noble one, whoever listens to this sūtra will progress irreversibly to the highest, most complete enlightenment.
{{milestone:{label:6.142,id:UT22084-089-013-874}}}“Why is that? {{page:{number:96,id:UT22084-089-013-3047,folio:F.199.a}}} Noble one, it ripens the supreme roots of merit of the bodhisattvas who are irreversibly upon the bhūmis, it is the sublime seal of the Dharma, and it is the king of all sūtras. Therefore, it should be listened to, obtained, read, and recited.
{{milestone:{label:6.143,id:UT22084-089-013-875}}}“Noble one, beings who have not planted roots of merit, who have not ripened their roots of merit, and who have not served many buddhas will not be able to hear this sublime Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:6.144,id:UT22084-089-013-876}}}“Noble one, just by hearing this Dharma teaching, noble sons or noble daughters will have a higher motivation and will never be apart from seeing the buddhas. They will never be apart from hearing the sublime Dharma. They will never be apart from honoring the saṅgha. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī of the accomplishment of the unceasing seal of the ocean. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī of engaging in the motivations, conduct, and languages of beings. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī of the shining crest of the sun. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī of accomplishing the suppression of all that arises. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī that is as hard as a vajra and destroys mountains. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī that enters into the teaching of the inexpressible meaning. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī that engages in all languages. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī that applies the seal of the accomplishment of the stainless domain of space. They will never be apart from the dhāraṇī that accomplishes the complete, infinite body of a buddha.
{{milestone:{label:6.145,id:UT22084-089-013-877}}}“Son of the devas, through obtaining these dhāraṇīs, the bodhisattvas emanate buddha bodies into the buddha realms in the ten directions and teach the Dharma. {{page:{number:97,id:UT22084-089-013-3048,folio:F.199.b}}} They will not deviate from the true nature, with no going and no coming. They will ripen beings without having a perception of beings. They will teach the Dharma without deviating from the sameness of all words. Although they manifest death and birth, they do not pass away, and have no birth. Because they have no thoughts toward all phenomena, that which is composite does not go anywhere and does not come from anywhere.”
{{milestone:{label:6.146,id:UT22084-089-013-878}}}When this Dharma teaching was given, three thousand bodhisattvas attained patience toward the quality of birthlessness; innumerable bodhisattvas became irreversible from the enlightenment mind; innumerable bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs attained the pure Dharma eyes for the Dharma; and innumerable beings developed the aspiration for the highest, most complete enlightenment.
{{milestone:{label:6.147,id:UT22084-089-013-879}}}Then, at that time, the Bhagavat recited this verse:
{{milestone:{label:6.148,id:UT22084-089-013-880}}}“This sublime Dharma that stops saṃsāra
Is profound, subtle, and difficult to see.
Those who are blind, obscured by desire,
Will not see it and will acquire suffering.”
{{milestone:{label:6.149,id:UT22084-089-013-882}}}That gathered assembly then rose from their seats, bowed their heads to the Bhagavat’s feet, and said, “Bhagavat, we will go to where someone is reading, reciting, or teaching this Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light, and we will form the assembly for that Dharma teacher and will benefit him, bestow happiness upon him, and make him physically and mentally happy. We will, with single-pointed minds, make offerings to him, and we will satisfy with happiness the assembly that listens to him. In the land of that king there will be no suffering because of fear of invading enemies, violence, or the anxiety of famine. The people will multiply and spread. {{page:{number:98,id:UT22084-089-013-3049,folio:F.200.a}}} Why is that? We will make offerings as to a stūpa, with parasols, banners, flowers, incense, and ornaments, to this place where the Dharma is taught. We will always protect it so that it will not deteriorate.”
{{milestone:{label:6.150,id:UT22084-089-013-883}}}Then the Bhagavat said to that gathered assembly, “Noble ones, be diligent in accomplishing this sublime sūtra, and this sublime Dharma will remain for a long time in this world.”
{{milestone:{label:6.151,id:UT22084-089-013-884}}}This concludes “The Purification of the Bhūmis,” the sixth chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:7,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-7}}}Chapter 7: A Praise of All the Realms of the Past, Future, and Present Samyaksaṃbuddhas
{{milestone:{label:7.2,id:UT22084-089-013-886}}}Then the Bhagavat said to the noble goddess Bodhisattvasamuccayā, “Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, there was a king by the name of Suvarṇabhujendra. Through this praise of all the tathāgatas, The Source of Lotus Flowers, he praised the buddha bhagavats of the past, future, and present. 
{{milestone:{label:7.3,id:UT22084-089-013-887}}}“ ‘The jinas who have appeared in the past, 
And the jinas present in worlds in the ten directions,
I pay homage to those jinas
And I praise all those jinas.{{note:{index:150,id:UT22084-089-013-888}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.4,id:UT22084-089-013-889}}}“ ‘A lord of munis is peaceful, totally peaceful, and pure.
His body is a perfect golden color.{{note:{index:151,id:UT22084-089-013-890}}}
A buddha’s speech is pleasant with every utterance,{{note:{index:152,id:UT22084-089-013-891}}}
A speech that resounds like the voice of Brahmā.
{{milestone:{label:7.5,id:UT22084-089-013-892}}}“ ‘He has hair{{note:{index:153,id:UT22084-089-013-893}}} like a bee, a peacock, and a blue lotus,{{note:{index:154,id:UT22084-089-013-894}}}
With dark blue curls{{note:{index:155,id:UT22084-089-013-895}}} like the blue jaybird.{{note:{index:156,id:UT22084-089-013-896}}}
His teeth are pure white like snow or a conch, 
And he is {{note:{index:157,id:UT22084-089-013-897}}} always beautiful like gold.
{{milestone:{label:7.6,id:UT22084-089-013-898}}}“ ‘His eyes are long, dark blue, and stainless; {{page:{number:99,id:UT22084-089-013-3050,folio:F.200.b}}}
They are like blossomed blue lotuses.
His broad, excellent tongue is the color of a red lotus,
Glowing like a red lotus, like red-lotus anthers.{{note:{index:158,id:UT22084-089-013-899}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.7,id:UT22084-089-013-900}}}“ ‘The ūrṇā hair on his face is the color of a conch or lotus root;{{note:{index:159,id:UT22084-089-013-901}}}
It curls to the right and is the color of white beryl.
The Muni’s body{{note:{index:160,id:UT22084-089-013-902}}} is like a sliver of the moon, 
The Muni’s crescent eyes{{note:{index:161,id:UT22084-089-013-903}}} are the color of a carpenter bee.{{note:{index:162,id:UT22084-089-013-904}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.8,id:UT22084-089-013-905}}}“ ‘His face has a high nose that is always prominent{{note:{index:163,id:UT22084-089-013-906}}}
And is soft and an excellent color, like bright gold.
He always, continuously, has the perfect nose{{note:{index:164,id:UT22084-089-013-907}}} of all the jinas,
Which is soft, sublime, supreme, and noble.
{{milestone:{label:7.9,id:UT22084-089-013-908}}}“ ‘From each and every pore there 
Rises a hair that curls to the right,
A dark blue, shining, gleaming curl,
Blue and beautiful like a peacock’s neck.
{{milestone:{label:7.10,id:UT22084-089-013-909}}}“ ‘As soon as he was born, his body shone,
Filling{{note:{index:165,id:UT22084-089-013-910}}} all worlds in the ten directions with light,
Ending the endless sufferings in the three worlds,
And satisfying beings with every happiness.
{{milestone:{label:7.11,id:UT22084-089-013-911}}}“ ‘He satisfied with happiness
The beings in the hells, animals,
Pretas, devas,{{note:{index:166,id:UT22084-089-013-912}}} and human beings,
And brought to an end all lower existences.
{{milestone:{label:7.12,id:UT22084-089-013-913}}}“ ‘His light was the excellent color of gold;
His body shone like purified gold.
His perfectly stainless face is a sugata moon,{{note:{index:167,id:UT22084-089-013-914}}}
His stainless mouth smiling beautifully.
{{milestone:{label:7.13,id:UT22084-089-013-915}}}“ ‘His body and limbs are soft like a young boy’s.
He has a perfect, powerful stride like a lion’s.
He has long hands and very long arms 
Like vines on a sal tree moved by the breeze.
{{milestone:{label:7.14,id:UT22084-089-013-916}}}“ ‘He has a fathom-wide aura that radiates light;
He is as bright as a thousand suns.
The stainless, supreme body of the lord of munis 
Illuminates all of the infinite realms.
{{milestone:{label:7.15,id:UT22084-089-013-917}}}“ ‘A multitude of night-bringing{{note:{index:168,id:UT22084-089-013-918}}} moons and suns, 
In endless hundreds of thousands of realms,
All become eclipsed by
The brilliant light of the Buddha.
{{milestone:{label:7.16,id:UT22084-089-013-919}}}“ ‘In endless hundreds of thousands of realms {{page:{number:100,id:UT22084-089-013-3051,folio:F.201.a}}}
May beings see{{note:{index:169,id:UT22084-089-013-920}}} the tathāgata suns— 
The suns of the buddhas, the lamps of worlds—
As a hundred thousand buddha suns.{{note:{index:170,id:UT22084-089-013-921}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.17,id:UT22084-089-013-922}}}“ ‘His body is endowed with a hundred thousand merits.
His body is adorned by all good qualities.
The Jina’s arms are like the trunk of the king of elephants.
His hands and feet are beautiful with stainless light.{{note:{index:171,id:UT22084-089-013-923}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.18,id:UT22084-089-013-924}}}“ ‘The buddhas who have been, who are as numerous as atoms,
Who are as numerous as the dust on the surface of the earth;
Those who are will be, who are as numerous as atoms;
And those who are present, who are as numerous as atoms—
{{milestone:{label:7.19,id:UT22084-089-013-925}}}“ ‘To those jinas I pay homage
In pure faith, with body and speech,
Offering flowers and offering perfumes,
And with a hundred praises and a virtuous mind.
{{milestone:{label:7.20,id:UT22084-089-013-926}}}“ ‘The good qualities that the jinas have
Are a manifold multitude of the very best.
I could not describe those qualities of the jinas{{note:{index:172,id:UT22084-089-013-927}}}
In a thousand eons with a hundred tongues.
{{milestone:{label:7.21,id:UT22084-089-013-928}}}“ ‘With a thousand tongues I could not describe
Even a fraction of the qualities of a single jina,
So how could I describe with a thousand tongues
The qualities of all the jinas?
{{milestone:{label:7.22,id:UT22084-089-013-929}}}“ ‘If the world and its paradises became an ocean,
And up to the summit of existence became filled with water,
It would be possible to measure that with the tip of a hair,
But one cannot measure a single quality of the sugatas.
{{milestone:{label:7.23,id:UT22084-089-013-930}}}“ ‘With faith and with body, speech, and mind
I praise and eulogize all the jinas. 
Through my accumulated perfect results of merit, 
May beings reach the state of buddhahood.’{{note:{index:173,id:UT22084-089-013-931}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.24,id:UT22084-089-013-932}}}“When the king had praised the Buddha in that way,
The king prayed in this way:
‘Wherever I am born,
In endless future eons,
{{milestone:{label:7.25,id:UT22084-089-013-933}}} “ ‘May I see such a drum{{note:{index:174,id:UT22084-089-013-934}}} in a dream.
There, may I hear this kind of confession.
May I encounter in every lifetime
A praise such as this Source of Lotuses.{{note:{index:175,id:UT22084-089-013-935}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.26,id:UT22084-089-013-936}}} “ ‘May I hear in a dream of those
Infinite, unequaled qualities of the buddhas,
Which are difficult to acquire even in a thousand eons, {{page:{number:101,id:UT22084-089-013-3052,folio:F.201.b}}}
And may I teach them when I am awake.
{{milestone:{label:7.27,id:UT22084-089-013-937}}} “ ‘May I free beings from the ocean of suffering.
May I complete the six perfections
And afterward attain the highest enlightenment,
And may my realm be without an equal.{{note:{index:176,id:UT22084-089-013-938}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.28,id:UT22084-089-013-939}}}“ ‘Through the ripened result of offering a drum,
And through the cause that is praising the buddhas,
May I directly see the Śākya lord of munis,
And may I attain there the prophecy of my buddhahood. 
{{milestone:{label:7.29,id:UT22084-089-013-940}}}“ ‘May these two youths, my two sons,
Kanakabhujendra and Kanaka­prabhā­svara, 
Attain there the prophecy
Of attaining the highest enlightenment.
{{milestone:{label:7.30,id:UT22084-089-013-941}}}“ ‘May those beings who have no protector or savior,
Who are without a refuge and are in distress,
May they all in the future 
Have saviors, protectors, and refuges.
{{milestone:{label:7.31,id:UT22084-089-013-942}}}“ ‘May the source of all suffering come to an end.
May there be the source of all happiness.{{note:{index:177,id:UT22084-089-013-943}}}
May I have the conduct of enlightenment in future eons,
Which are as numerous as the eons of the past.
{{milestone:{label:7.32,id:UT22084-089-013-944}}}“ ‘Through the confession of The Sublime Golden Light,
May my ocean of bad actions dry up, 
May my ocean of karma come to an end,
And may my ocean of kleśas cease to exist.
{{milestone:{label:7.33,id:UT22084-089-013-945}}}“ ‘May my ocean of merit become complete.
Through the power of the light of stainless wisdom,
May the ocean of my wisdom become complete
And may there be an ocean of all qualities.{{note:{index:178,id:UT22084-089-013-946}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.34,id:UT22084-089-013-947}}}“ ‘May the qualities of enlightenment be complete.{{note:{index:179,id:UT22084-089-013-948}}}
Through the power of The Sublime Golden Light confession, 
May my merit become radiant.{{note:{index:180,id:UT22084-089-013-949}}}
May the light of my enlightenment be purified.
{{milestone:{label:7.35,id:UT22084-089-013-950}}}“ ‘Through the sublime light of stainless wisdom,{{note:{index:181,id:UT22084-089-013-951}}}
May my body shine with light.
In order that the light of merit be bright,
May I become preeminent within the three worlds.
{{milestone:{label:7.36,id:UT22084-089-013-952}}}“ ‘May I always have the power of merit.{{note:{index:182,id:UT22084-089-013-953}}}
May I be liberated from the ocean of suffering {{page:{number:102,id:UT22084-089-013-3053,folio:F.202.a}}}
And practice enlightened conduct in future eons
With every happiness that is like an ocean.
{{milestone:{label:7.37,id:UT22084-089-013-954}}}“ ‘In future times, may my realm 
Have the same infinite qualities 
As the superior, infinite qualities
Of all the jinas in the realms
That have been in the three worlds in the past.’{{note:{index:183,id:UT22084-089-013-955}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.38,id:UT22084-089-013-956}}}“Ruciraketu, you should know
That King Suvarṇabhujendra, 
Who made this prayer in the past,
Has become you in this present time.
{{milestone:{label:7.39,id:UT22084-089-013-957}}}“Your two sons in the past,
Kanakabhujendra and Kanaka­prabhā­svara,
Are now Rūpyaketu and Rūpyaprabha
I made that prophecy at that time.”
{{milestone:{label:7.40,id:UT22084-089-013-958}}}The vast assembly, on hearing that,
All developed the enlightenment mind.
“May we now and in all future times
Always make this confession!” {{note:{index:184,id:UT22084-089-013-959}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.41,id:UT22084-089-013-960}}}This concludes “A Praise of All the Realms of the Past, Future, and Present Samyaksaṃbuddhas,” the seventh chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:8,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-8}}}Chapter 8: The Dhāraṇī Called Golden
{{milestone:{label:8.1,id:UT22084-089-013-962}}}Then the Bhagavat said to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sukhavihāra within that assembly, “Noble one, any noble man or noble woman who wishes to make an offering to all the buddhas of the past, the future, and the present should carry and possess this dhāraṇī that is called golden. Why is that? It is because this dhāraṇī is the mother of the past, future, and present buddha bhagavats. One who possesses this dhāraṇī will greatly increase their accumulation of merit. Those who planted roots of merit with countless bhagavats of the past will possess and hold this dhāraṇī. Those who have pure, faultless conduct without deterioration {{page:{number:103,id:UT22084-089-013-3054,folio:F.202.b}}} will be able to enter this extremely profound Dharma teaching.”
{{milestone:{label:8.2,id:UT22084-089-013-963}}}Then the Bhagavat said, “This is the rite for practicing the dhāraṇī-mantra: Recite these names of past buddha bhagavats and bodhisattvas and with a one-pointed mind, pay homage to them, and then recite the mantra:
{{milestone:{label:8.3,id:UT22084-089-013-964}}}“I pay homage to all the buddhas in the ten directions,
{{milestone:{label:8.4,id:UT22084-089-013-965}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattvas.
{{milestone:{label:8.5,id:UT22084-089-013-966}}}“I pay homage to all the śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, and āryas.
{{milestone:{label:8.6,id:UT22084-089-013-967}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Śākyamuni.
{{milestone:{label:8.7,id:UT22084-089-013-968}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Akṣobhya in the east.
{{milestone:{label:8.8,id:UT22084-089-013-969}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Ratnaketu in the south.
{{milestone:{label:8.9,id:UT22084-089-013-970}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Amitābha in the west.
{{milestone:{label:8.10,id:UT22084-089-013-971}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Dundubhisvara in the north.
{{milestone:{label:8.11,id:UT22084-089-013-972}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Viśālaśrī above.
{{milestone:{label:8.12,id:UT22084-089-013-973}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Varaprabha below.
{{milestone:{label:8.13,id:UT22084-089-013-974}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Ratnagarbha.
{{milestone:{label:8.14,id:UT22084-089-013-975}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Samantaprabha. 
{{milestone:{label:8.15,id:UT22084-089-013-976}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Samantāvabhāsa. 
{{milestone:{label:8.16,id:UT22084-089-013-977}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Supreme Incense Heap. 
{{milestone:{label:8.17,id:UT22084-089-013-978}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Excellent Lotus. 
{{milestone:{label:8.18,id:UT22084-089-013-979}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Equally Seeing. 
{{milestone:{label:8.19,id:UT22084-089-013-980}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Ratnaśikhin. 
{{milestone:{label:8.20,id:UT22084-089-013-981}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Highest Jewels. 
{{milestone:{label:8.21,id:UT22084-089-013-982}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Ratnaprabha. 
{{milestone:{label:8.22,id:UT22084-089-013-983}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Courageous Established Intention.
{{milestone:{label:8.23,id:UT22084-089-013-984}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Completely Pure Moonlight Sign Renowned King.
{{milestone:{label:8.24,id:UT22084-089-013-985}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Radiant Flower Display. 
{{milestone:{label:8.25,id:UT22084-089-013-986}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Aṃśurāja. 
{{milestone:{label:8.26,id:UT22084-089-013-987}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Renowned King Virtuous Stainless Light. {{page:{number:104,id:UT22084-089-013-3055,folio:F.203.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:8.27,id:UT22084-089-013-988}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Avalokiteśvarābhaya. 
{{milestone:{label:8.28,id:UT22084-089-013-989}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Abhayakīrti. 
{{milestone:{label:8.29,id:UT22084-089-013-990}}}“I pay homage to the Buddha Supreme King. 
{{milestone:{label:8.30,id:UT22084-089-013-991}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Avalokiteśvara.
{{milestone:{label:8.31,id:UT22084-089-013-992}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣitigarbha.
{{milestone:{label:8.32,id:UT22084-089-013-993}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Ākāśagarbha.
{{milestone:{label:8.33,id:UT22084-089-013-994}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Mañjuśrī.
{{milestone:{label:8.34,id:UT22084-089-013-995}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Vajrapāṇi. 
{{milestone:{label:8.35,id:UT22084-089-013-996}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Samantabhadra. 
{{milestone:{label:8.36,id:UT22084-089-013-997}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Akṣayamati. 
{{milestone:{label:8.37,id:UT22084-089-013-998}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Mahāsthāmaprāpta. 
{{milestone:{label:8.38,id:UT22084-089-013-999}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya.
{{milestone:{label:8.39,id:UT22084-089-013-1000}}}“I pay homage to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sumati. 
{{milestone:{label:8.40,id:UT22084-089-013-1001}}}“Having paid homage to them, recite this dhāraṇī: 
{{milestone:{label:8.41,id:UT22084-089-013-1002}}}namo ratnatrayāya | tadyathā | kuṭi kuṭini imirito koṣaṇi imiriṇi irī svāha |
{{milestone:{label:8.42,id:UT22084-089-013-1003}}}Then the Bhagavat said to the bodhisattva Sukhavihāra, “This dhāraṇī is the mother of the buddhas in the three times. Therefore, any noble man or noble woman who carries and possesses this dhāraṇī will increase their accumulation of merit immeasurably, incalculably. They will have revered, made offerings to, served, and praised countless buddhas. Those buddhas will give them the prophecy of their attainment of the highest, most complete enlightenment. 
{{milestone:{label:8.43,id:UT22084-089-013-1004}}}“Sukhavihāra, those who carry this dhāraṇī-mantra will attain the fulfillment of their wishes, such as clothes, alms, {{page:{number:105,id:UT22084-089-013-3056,folio:F.203.b}}} jewels, becoming learned and wise, becoming healthy, and having a long life, and their merit will increase greatly. Whatever they wish for will all be accomplished.
{{milestone:{label:8.44,id:UT22084-089-013-1005}}}“Sukhavihāra, if this mantra is carried and possessed until the attainment of the highest, most complete enlightenment, one will always be in the company of the bodhisattva Golden City Mountain, the bodhisattva Maitreya, the bodhisattva Sāgara, the bodhisattva Samantāvalokiteśvara, the bodhisattva Mañjuśrī, the bodhisattva Mahāpiṅgala, and so on. Those bodhisattvas will protect them. 
{{milestone:{label:8.45,id:UT22084-089-013-1006}}}“Sukhavihāra, know that this is the rite for accomplishing this dhāraṇī. For the first repetition, one should perform a propitiation by repeating it ten thousand and eight times. Then one should make a maṇḍala inside a solitary building and, on the sixteenth day of the month, wash, put on new clothes, and make offerings with parasols, flowers, various kinds of food, and so on, placing them inside the maṇḍala. At the beginning, as previously described, one should recite the names of the buddhas and bodhisattvas, and then pay homage with veneration and confess bad actions. One should then kneel with the right knee on the ground, repeat that mantra a thousand and eight times, and then sit up straight and think about what one wishes for. Then, before the sun rises, eat one pure meal within the maṇḍala. When someone comes out from that maṇḍala after fifteen days have passed, they will have inconceivable power, merit, and majesty, and all their wishes will be fulfilled. 
{{milestone:{label:8.46,id:UT22084-089-013-1007}}}“If their wishes are not fulfilled, they should reenter that maṇḍala {{page:{number:106,id:UT22084-089-013-3057,folio:F.204.a}}} and then their wishes will be fulfilled. From then on, they should always remember this.”
{{milestone:{label:8.47,id:UT22084-089-013-1008}}}This concludes “The Dhāraṇī Called Golden,” the eighth chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:9,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-9}}}Chapter 9: Emptiness
{{milestone:{label:9.1,id:UT22084-089-013-1010}}}Then the Bhagavat, having taught that dhāraṇī, in order to benefit and bring happiness to that gathered assembly of bodhisattva mahāsattvas, devas, humans, and so on, and in order to teach the characteristics of the ultimate truth, emptiness, recited these verses:
{{milestone:{label:9.2,id:UT22084-089-013-1011}}}“I have taught the Dharmas of emptiness 
Very extensively in countless other sūtras.
Therefore, in this supreme sūtra, 
I will teach the Dharmas of emptiness briefly.
{{milestone:{label:9.3,id:UT22084-089-013-1012}}}“Unknowing beings with little intelligence 
Are not able to know all the Dharmas.
Therefore, in this supreme sūtra 
I will teach the Dharmas of emptiness briefly.
{{milestone:{label:9.4,id:UT22084-089-013-1013}}}“I teach this lord of supreme sūtras
Through other methods, ways, and causes,
And through compassion, so that all beings will understand 
And so that it will arise in beings.{{note:{index:185,id:UT22084-089-013-1014}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.5,id:UT22084-089-013-1015}}}“This body is like an empty village.
The senses are like six village{{note:{index:186,id:UT22084-089-013-1016}}} thieves, 
Who, although they are in the same village,
Are not aware of one another.
{{milestone:{label:9.6,id:UT22084-089-013-1017}}}“The sense of sight runs toward forms;
The sense of hearing moves after sounds;
The sense of smell steals various aromas;
The sense of taste runs after flavors;
{{milestone:{label:9.7,id:UT22084-089-013-1018}}}“The sense of touch pursues tactility;
The mental sense investigates phenomena.
These six senses in relation to one another
Are each engaging with their own objects of perception.
{{milestone:{label:9.8,id:UT22084-089-013-1019}}}“The mind is unstable, like an illusion.
The six senses experience their fields of perception,
The six village{{note:{index:187,id:UT22084-089-013-1020}}} thieves present there
Are like a man running around in an empty village.
{{milestone:{label:9.9,id:UT22084-089-013-1021}}}“Just as the mind and the six present senses {{page:{number:107,id:UT22084-089-013-3058,folio:F.204.b}}}
Know the range of sensory perception—
Forms, sounds, and likewise smells,
Flavors, tactility, and the range of mental phenomena—
{{milestone:{label:9.10,id:UT22084-089-013-1022}}}“The mind enters the senses, moving like a bird 
Throughout all six of them.
In whatever sense it is present,
It has the nature of that sense’s perception.{{note:{index:188,id:UT22084-089-013-1023}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.11,id:UT22084-089-013-1024}}}“The body is unmoving and has no activity. 
It has no essence and arises from conditions.
It has no real existence but arises from concepts.
It is an empty village; it is like a working machine.
{{milestone:{label:9.12,id:UT22084-089-013-1025}}}“Earth, fire, water, and air
Dwell here and there outside the village.{{note:{index:189,id:UT22084-089-013-1026}}}
They are like poisonous snakes in one location
That are always in conflict with one another.
{{milestone:{label:9.13,id:UT22084-089-013-1027}}}“Of those four snakes of the elements,
Two move upward and two go downward;
They go in twos to the main and intermediate directions,
And all those element snakes are destroyed.
{{milestone:{label:9.14,id:UT22084-089-013-1028}}}“The earth snake and the water snake—
These two come to an end below.
The fire snake and the air snake—
They go upward into the sky.
{{milestone:{label:9.15,id:UT22084-089-013-1029}}}“The mind and the consciousnesses remain,
And they go according to previous karma.
According to the karma created in the past, they are reborn
Into an existence among devas, humans, or the three lower realms.
{{milestone:{label:9.16,id:UT22084-089-013-1030}}}“When the phlegm, air, and bile come to an end,
The body becomes covered with urine and vomit.{{note:{index:190,id:UT22084-089-013-1031}}}
It becomes a disgusting mass of worms 
And is cast into the charnel ground as if it were wood.
{{milestone:{label:9.17,id:UT22084-089-013-1032}}}“Goddess, look at these phenomena,
At whatever being or individual is here;
All of these phenomena are empty,
But they occur through the factor of ignorance.
{{milestone:{label:9.18,id:UT22084-089-013-1033}}}“All these great elements{{note:{index:191,id:UT22084-089-013-1034}}} are not ‘great occurrences.’
They occur through nonoccurrence and so do not occur. 
Because the occurring elements are nonoccurring,
For that reason I call them ‘great elements.’{{note:{index:192,id:UT22084-089-013-1035}}}{{page:{number:108,id:UT22084-089-013-3059,folio:F.205.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.19,id:UT22084-089-013-1036}}}“They are not existent and never were existent.
They come to be because of ignorance.
This ignorance, too, is not existent.{{note:{index:193,id:UT22084-089-013-1037}}}
Therefore, I teach that this is ignorance.
{{milestone:{label:9.20,id:UT22084-089-013-1038}}}“Formations, consciousness, and name and form;
The six āyatanas, contact, and sensation;
Craving, grasping and likewise becoming;
And the misfortunes of birth, aging, death, and misery—
{{milestone:{label:9.21,id:UT22084-089-013-1039}}}“Those inconceivable sufferings in saṃsāra
That are present in the wheel of saṃsāra
Have happened without happening and have no origination.
The distinctions made by an erroneous mind,
{{milestone:{label:9.22,id:UT22084-089-013-1040}}}“And the view that there is a self, should be cut through.
Cut through the net of the kleśas with the sword of wisdom. 
See that the basis of the skandhas is empty.
Reach the vast qualities of the buddhas.
{{milestone:{label:9.23,id:UT22084-089-013-1041}}}“I have opened the gate of the city of amṛta. 
I have shown everyone the vessel of amṛta liquid.
I have entered the place that is the city{{note:{index:194,id:UT22084-089-013-1042}}} of amṛta,
And I have been satiated by the amṛta liquid.
{{milestone:{label:9.24,id:UT22084-089-013-1043}}}“I have beaten the sublime great drum{{note:{index:195,id:UT22084-089-013-1044}}} of the Dharma
I have blown the sublime conch of the Dharma.
I have lit the sublime lamp of the Dharma,
And I have sent down a sublime rain of Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:9.25,id:UT22084-089-013-1045}}}“I have defeated the supreme enemy, the kleśas.
I have raised the sublime banner of the Dharma.
I have brought beings across the ocean of existence.
I have blocked the road to the three lower existences.
{{milestone:{label:9.26,id:UT22084-089-013-1046}}}“There are beings who are tormented by the fire of the kleśas,
Who have no support or protector.
I have extinguished the fire of the kleśas in those beings
And brought them relief with the cooling liquid of amṛta.{{note:{index:196,id:UT22084-089-013-1047}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.27,id:UT22084-089-013-1048}}}“For that reason, through many past eons
I made offerings to innumerable guides,{{note:{index:197,id:UT22084-089-013-1049}}}
And in seeking for the Dharma body
I practiced resolute discipline for the sake of enlightenment.
{{milestone:{label:9.28,id:UT22084-089-013-1050}}}“I gave away my arms, eyes, and legs,
My head,{{note:{index:198,id:UT22084-089-013-1051}}} beloved sons and daughters,
Wealth, treasures, ornamentations of jewels and pearls,
Gold, beryl, and various kinds of jewels.
{{milestone:{label:9.29,id:UT22084-089-013-1052}}}“If all the trees in the trichiliocosm, 
And all the grasses, the plants,
And the forests—everything that {{page:{number:109,id:UT22084-089-013-3060,folio:F.205.b}}}
Grows from the ground—were to be cut down,{{note:{index:199,id:UT22084-089-013-1053}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.30,id:UT22084-089-013-1054}}}“And they were all ground down
And made into the smallest atoms
And were formed into a heap of powder
That reached the domain of the sky,
{{milestone:{label:9.31,id:UT22084-089-013-1055}}}“It would not be possible to divide that into portions.{{note:{index:200,id:UT22084-089-013-1056}}}
There are the particles that exist in the earth—
The countless elemental particles 
In all the trichiliocosm worlds—
{{milestone:{label:9.32,id:UT22084-089-013-1057}}}And if the knowledge of all beings
Could become that of a single being,
Such that with that knowledge
All those particles could be counted,
{{milestone:{label:9.33,id:UT22084-089-013-1058}}}“Then the humans with that perfect wisdom,{{note:{index:201,id:UT22084-089-013-1059}}}
Who would be superior to all other beings,
Could possibly count all those particles,
But they would not be able to calculate a jina’s wisdom.
{{milestone:{label:9.34,id:UT22084-089-013-1060}}}“If they were to engage with a single instant 
Of the wisdom of the great Muni
For many millions of eons,
They would still be unable to calculate it.”
{{milestone:{label:9.35,id:UT22084-089-013-1061}}}This concludes “Emptiness,” the ninth chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:10,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-10}}}Chapter 10: Fulfilling Wishes on the Basis of Emptiness
{{milestone:{label:10.1,id:UT22084-089-013-1063}}}On hearing that very profound Dharma teaching, the goddess Ratnārcī was delighted and overjoyed. She rose from her seat, and, with her upper robe over one shoulder, knelt on her right knee, placed her palms together in homage, bowed toward the Bhagavat, and in order to ask how to practice this profound teaching, spoke these verses to the Bhagavat:
{{milestone:{label:10.2,id:UT22084-089-013-1064}}}“Jina, supreme two-legged being
Who completely illuminates the world,
I pray that with compassion you teach me 
The correct way of enlightened conduct.”
{{milestone:{label:10.3,id:UT22084-089-013-1065}}}He replied to the noble goddess:
{{milestone:{label:10.4,id:UT22084-089-013-1066}}} “Whatever doubts you have, 
Ask questions about that meaning
And I will elucidate and teach it.”
{{milestone:{label:10.5,id:UT22084-089-013-1067}}}Then the noble goddess said to the Bhagavat:
{{milestone:{label:10.6,id:UT22084-089-013-1068}}}“For the benefit of myself and others:
How do the bodhisattvas
Practice the enlightened conduct
That is free of saṃsāra and nirvāṇa?” {{page:{number:110,id:UT22084-089-013-3061,folio:F.206.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:10.7,id:UT22084-089-013-1069}}}The Bhagavat then said to the noble goddess:
{{milestone:{label:10.8,id:UT22084-089-013-1070}}}“Goddess, be dedicated to sameness 
Through practicing enlightened conduct
While dwelling in the Dharma realm.”
That is what he said to her.{{note:{index:202,id:UT22084-089-013-1071}}}
{{milestone:{label:10.9,id:UT22084-089-013-1072}}}The noble goddess asked the Bhagavat, “Bhagavat, how does one practice equanimity by performing enlightened conduct while dwelling in the Dharma realm?”
{{milestone:{label:10.10,id:UT22084-089-013-1073}}}“Goddess,” replied the Bhagavat, “the five skandhas are said to be the Dharma realm, and the Dharma realm is the five skandhas. However, one cannot say it is the five skandhas and one cannot say it is not the five skandhas. If the Dharma realm itself were the five skandhas, that would be nihilism. If one were to state that it is other than the five skandhas, that would be eternalism. It is devoid of both characteristics. It does not dwell in either of the two extremes. It cannot be viewed; it transcends being an object of view. It has no name or feature. That is what is called the Dharma realm.
{{milestone:{label:10.11,id:UT22084-089-013-1074}}}“Family goddess, why are the five skandhas called the Dharma realm? The five skandhas are not produced through causes and conditions. If they were produced by causes and conditions, they would be either that which has been produced that is being produced, or that which is not produced that is being produced. If they were a production of what has already been produced, it is logical that causes and conditions would not be needed. If they were that which is not produced that is being produced, then there would be no perceivable production. Why is that? Unproduced phenomena are not existent, and therefore they have no names and no features. They cannot be evaluated, measured, or described through examples. They are not produced by causes and conditions.
{{milestone:{label:10.12,id:UT22084-089-013-1075}}}“Noble goddess, a drumbeat originates through dependence on wood, skin, and a hand, but the drumbeat’s past is empty, its future is empty, and its present is empty. That drumbeat does not originate from the wood, and it does not originate from the skin or the hand. {{page:{number:111,id:UT22084-089-013-3062,folio:F.206.b}}} It is not produced by the three times. Therefore, it is not produced. That which is not produced does not cease. That which does not cease does not come from anywhere. That which does not come from anywhere does not go anywhere. That which does not go anywhere is neither eternal nor nothingness. It is neither one nor separate. Why is that? If the five skandhas were one with the Dharma realm, they would not be different from the Dharma realm. Then childlike, ordinary beings would perceive the ultimate truth and attain the sublime bliss of nirvāṇa. But it is not like that, so they are not one. 
{{milestone:{label:10.13,id:UT22084-089-013-1076}}}“If they were separate from the Dharma realm then the conduct of the buddhas and bodhisattvas would have their same characteristics and they would not become liberated from the bondage of the kleśas and they would not attain the highest, most complete enlightenment of buddhahood.
{{milestone:{label:10.14,id:UT22084-089-013-1077}}}“Why is that? It is because the āryas have the single nature of the composite and noncomposite, and therefore they are not different. Therefore, the five skandhas are neither existent nor nonexistent. They are neither produced by causes and conditions, nor not produced by causes and conditions. Words cannot reach this. It has no name or features. It has no cause or condition. It cannot be taught through examples. It is devoid of a beginning or an end. It is naturally empty. This is what the āryas know, but it is not within the field of experience of others. Therefore, the Dharma realm is taught through the five skandhas. 
{{milestone:{label:10.15,id:UT22084-089-013-1078}}}“Moreover, noble goddess, any noble son or noble daughter who wishes for the highest, most complete enlightenment, in which the ultimate and the relative are not anything other than each other, that is difficult to comprehend. The nature of the fields of experience of āryas and lower beings are not one, nor are they different. {{page:{number:112,id:UT22084-089-013-3063,folio:F.207.a}}} Therefore the conduct of enlightenment should be practiced based on the Dharma realm, without eliminating the relative, and without being apart from the ultimate.”
{{milestone:{label:10.16,id:UT22084-089-013-1079}}}When the Bhagavat said that, the noble goddess was delighted and happy. She rose from her seat, and, with her upper robe over one shoulder, knelt on her right knee, placed her palms together, bowed down her head in homage, and said to the Bhagavat, “Bhagavat, I will train in the bodhisattva conduct that the Bhagavat has taught.”
{{milestone:{label:10.17,id:UT22084-089-013-1080}}}Then Mahābrahmā, the lord of Sahā, who was among that gathered assembly, asked the noble goddess Ratnārcī, “Goddess, how are you going to master through practice this bodhisattva conduct that is difficult to accomplish?”
{{milestone:{label:10.18,id:UT22084-089-013-1081}}}The noble goddess replied to Mahābrahmā, “Great Brahmarāja, the meaning that the Bhagavat has taught is very profound, so that no ordinary being can know its meaning. It is the field of experience of āryas, and therefore it is supremely subtle and difficult to know. I will attain a state of bliss through relying on this Dharma.
