{{milestone:{label:19.16,id:UT22084-089-013-1730}}}The Bhagavat then congratulated Saṃjñeya, the great general of the yakṣas, saying, “It is excellent, excellent, that you have inconceivably increased your merit by speaking these mantra words in order to bring benefit and happiness to all beings and to protect this sublime Dharma.”
{{milestone:{label:19.17,id:UT22084-089-013-1731}}}This concludes “Saṃjñeya, the Lord of Yakṣas,” the nineteenth chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:20,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-20}}}Chapter 20: The King’s Treatise: The Commitment of the Lord of Devas
{{milestone:{label:20.1,id:UT22084-089-013-1733}}}Then Dṛḍhā, the goddess of the earth, who was seated within that great assembly, rose from her seat, bowed down her head to the Bhagavat’s feet, and then, with her palms placed together, said to the Bhagavat, “Bhagavat, if in any land there is a human king who does not practice the true Dharma, {{page:{number:193,id:UT22084-089-013-3144,folio:F.247.b}}} he will not remain long ruling that land or bringing happiness to many beings through a prestigious reign.
{{milestone:{label:20.2,id:UT22084-089-013-1734}}}“Bhagavat, I pray that because you are compassionate you will, with a treatise on kingship, teach how to rule over a land. Through hearing such a Dharma, human kings will be able to remain for a long time in sublime sovereignty, protecting the world, and all the people in that land will become completely happy.”
{{milestone:{label:20.3,id:UT22084-089-013-1735}}}Then the Bhagavat, in the midst of that great assembly, said to the goddess of the earth, “Goddess of the earth, for that reason listen very well. In the past, in a time gone by, there was a king by the name of Balendraketu,{{note:{index:408,id:UT22084-089-013-1736}}} who had a son by the name of Ruciraketu. Not long after Ruciraketu’s royal consecration, Balendraketu said to him, ‘I received from my father, the supreme king Pinnacle of Lords,{{note:{index:409,id:UT22084-089-013-1737}}} the treatise on kingship called The Commitment of the Lord of Devas. I have, up until now, ruled for twenty thousand years in accordance with the treatise on kingship called The Commitment of the Lord of Devas. Up until now, I have not been known to follow any ways that are not the Dharma for even an instant. So, son, what is the treatise on kingship called The Commitment of the Lord of Devas?’
{{milestone:{label:20.4,id:UT22084-089-013-1738}}}“Then, at that time, in that time, noble goddess, King Balendraketu taught extensively, through these verses, the treatise on kingship, The Commitment of the Lord of Devas, to his son King Ruciraketu:
{{milestone:{label:20.5,id:UT22084-089-013-1739}}}“ ‘I will teach the treatise on kingship
That benefits all beings,
Cuts through all doubts,
And destroys all wrongdoing.
{{milestone:{label:20.6,id:UT22084-089-013-1740}}}“ ‘Each and every king,
Have a joyful mind!
And with palms together, listen to
All the commitments of the lord of devas.
{{milestone:{label:20.7,id:UT22084-089-013-1741}}}“ ‘On this lord of mountains, Vajraprākāra,
The lords of the devas assembled,
And the protectors of the world stood up
In order to question the lord of Brahmās: {{page:{number:194,id:UT22084-089-013-3145,folio:F.248.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.8,id:UT22084-089-013-1742}}}“ ‘ “You, Brahmā, the principal deity,
The one who is the lord over all devas,
We pray that you cut through our doubts
And cut through our concerns.
{{milestone:{label:20.9,id:UT22084-089-013-1743}}}“ ‘ “Why is a king, who has been born 
In the human world, called a deva?
For what reason is a king
Given the title of ‘son of the devas’?
{{milestone:{label:20.10,id:UT22084-089-013-1744}}}“ ‘ “If he is a deva, then why is it that
He is born into this world of humans,
Becomes a lord of humans,
And acts as a king for humans?” {{note:{index:410,id:UT22084-089-013-1745}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.11,id:UT22084-089-013-1746}}}“ ‘The protectors of the world asked
Those questions of the lord of Brahmās
And that principal deity, Brahmā,
Said these words to the protectors of the world:
{{milestone:{label:20.12,id:UT22084-089-013-1747}}}“ ‘ “The world protectors have thus
Asked me such questions,
So I will teach an excellent treatise
In order to bring benefit to beings.
{{milestone:{label:20.13,id:UT22084-089-013-1748}}}“ ‘ “I will describe the births 
Of kings within human existences
And the causes through which
They become the kings of their domains.
{{milestone:{label:20.14,id:UT22084-089-013-1749}}}“ ‘ “Blessed by the lords of devas,
He will enter the mother’s uterus.
First, he is blessed by the devas,
And afterward, he comes into the womb. 
{{milestone:{label:20.15,id:UT22084-089-013-1750}}}“ ‘ “Although born in the human world,
He becomes a lord of humans.
As he is born from the devas,
He is called ‘a son of the devas.’
{{milestone:{label:20.16,id:UT22084-089-013-1751}}}“ ‘ “The deva lords of Trāyastriṃśa state,
‘You are the child of all the devas.’
They bestow upon him the right to be king
And he emanates to become a lord of humans.
{{milestone:{label:20.17,id:UT22084-089-013-1752}}}“ ‘ “He brings to an end all evil acts 
And destroys that which is not Dharma.
He establishes beings in good works
In order to direct them to the paradises.
{{milestone:{label:20.18,id:UT22084-089-013-1753}}}“ ‘ “The lord of men, whether 
A human or a gandharva,
A caṇḍāla or a rākṣasa, 
Prevents wickedness. 
{{milestone:{label:20.19,id:UT22084-089-013-1754}}}“ ‘ “The lord of men is a father and mother
For those who engage in good actions.
He has been blessed by the kings of devas{{note:{index:411,id:UT22084-089-013-1755}}}
To teach them the ripening of results.
{{milestone:{label:20.20,id:UT22084-089-013-1756}}}“ ‘ “He has been blessed by the kings of devas{{note:{index:412,id:UT22084-089-013-1757}}}
In order to teach the ripened results
Of the karma of performing good actions
And performing bad actions in this life. {{page:{number:195,id:UT22084-089-013-3146,folio:F.248.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.21,id:UT22084-089-013-1758}}}“ ‘ “Whenever a king does nothing about
The wicked inhabitants in his realm,
Does not appropriately punish
The people who are guilty of bad acts,
{{milestone:{label:20.22,id:UT22084-089-013-1759}}}“ ‘ “And ignores the evils that are done,
Then unrighteousness will increase greatly,
Conflicts and dishonesty
Will subsequently arise in the land,
{{milestone:{label:20.23,id:UT22084-089-013-1760}}}“ ‘ “And the lords of devas{{note:{index:413,id:UT22084-089-013-1761}}} will be disturbed
Within their Trāyastriṃśa palace.
Whenever a king does nothing about
The wicked inhabitants in his realm,
{{milestone:{label:20.24,id:UT22084-089-013-1762}}}“ ‘ “Then there will be terrible dishonesty
And dreadful people will vanquish his land.
The armies of adversaries will invade
And will completely destroy that land,
{{milestone:{label:20.25,id:UT22084-089-013-1763}}}“ ‘ “And they will destroy property and families.
People will steal from one another,
Using many forms of dishonesty,
Whatever wealth has been accumulated.{{note:{index:414,id:UT22084-089-013-1764}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.26,id:UT22084-089-013-1765}}}“ ‘ “There are the duties of kingship,
And if those activities are not carried out,
Then he will destroy his own kingdom
Like a king of elephants destroys a pond.
{{milestone:{label:20.27,id:UT22084-089-013-1766}}}“ ‘ “Disastrous winds will blow,
Disastrous rains will fall,
And the sun, the moon, the planets, 
And lunar asterisms will bring disaster.
{{milestone:{label:20.28,id:UT22084-089-013-1767}}}“ ‘ “In the land where the king is impassive,
Seeds, harvests, flowers, and fruit
Will fail to ripen properly
And famines will occur.
{{milestone:{label:20.29,id:UT22084-089-013-1768}}}“ ‘ “Whenever a king does nothing about
The wicked inhabitants in his realm,
Then the devas in their palaces
Will at that time become displeased.{{note:{index:415,id:UT22084-089-013-1769}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.30,id:UT22084-089-013-1770}}}“ ‘ “All of those lords of devas
Will be saying to one another,
‘This king{{note:{index:416,id:UT22084-089-013-1771}}} has no righteousness;
He is on the side of unrighteousness.’
{{milestone:{label:20.31,id:UT22084-089-013-1772}}}“ ‘ “Such a king will before long
Cause the devas to be disturbed,
And because the devas are disturbed,
His kingdom will be completely destroyed.
{{milestone:{label:20.32,id:UT22084-089-013-1773}}}“ ‘ “Unrighteousness will arise in that land,
And it will also be destroyed by weapons.{{note:{index:417,id:UT22084-089-013-1774}}}
Dishonesty and conflicts
And also illness will arise.
{{milestone:{label:20.33,id:UT22084-089-013-1775}}}“ ‘ “The lords of devas will be enraged,
And the devas will abandon him.
The kingdom will be destroyed,
And the king will encounter misery.
{{milestone:{label:20.34,id:UT22084-089-013-1776}}}“ ‘ “He will be separated from those he loves,
Whether they be brothers or sons.
He will even be separated from his beloved wife,
Or it will be that his daughter will die. {{page:{number:196,id:UT22084-089-013-3147,folio:F.249.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.35,id:UT22084-089-013-3223}}}“ ‘ “There will be shooting stars that will fall,
And similarly there will appear comets,
And the armies of invading enemies,
And famines will drastically take place.
{{milestone:{label:20.36,id:UT22084-089-013-1777}}}“ ‘ “His cherished elephant and
Cherished minister will die.{{note:{index:418,id:UT22084-089-013-1778}}}
Afterward, his cherished 
Camels will also die.{{note:{index:419,id:UT22084-089-013-1779}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.37,id:UT22084-089-013-1780}}}“ ‘ “People will steal from one another
Homes, possessions, and wealth.
In this and that region they will
Strike{{note:{index:420,id:UT22084-089-013-1781}}} one another with weapons.
{{milestone:{label:20.38,id:UT22084-089-013-1782}}}“ ‘ “There will arise in those regions
Fighting, quarreling, and dishonesty.
A demon will enter the kingdom
And there will be dreadful illnesses. 
{{milestone:{label:20.39,id:UT22084-089-013-1783}}}“ ‘ “After that, even the recipients of
Offerings will become unrighteous.
His court and his ministers
Will also become unrighteous.
{{milestone:{label:20.40,id:UT22084-089-013-1784}}}“ ‘ “Those individuals who are righteous
Will constantly be punished.
If unrighteous individuals are honored
And the righteous are punished,
{{milestone:{label:20.41,id:UT22084-089-013-1785}}}“ ‘ “Because the malevolent are loved and honored,
And because the good are punished,
In that place water, lunar asterisms,
And wind, those three, will become agitated. 
{{milestone:{label:20.42,id:UT22084-089-013-3229}}}“ ‘ “If unrighteous beings are favored,
There are three things that will be destroyed:
The vital essence of the flavor of the Dharmas,
The vitality of beings, and the fecundity of the earth.
{{milestone:{label:20.43,id:UT22084-089-013-1786}}}“ ‘ “Through honoring evil people
And dishonoring good people,
There are three things that will occur:
Death, lightning, and famine.
{{milestone:{label:20.44,id:UT22084-089-013-1787}}}“ ‘ “Afterward, the vitality and flavor
Of fruits and harvests will vanish,{{note:{index:421,id:UT22084-089-013-1788}}}
And in those regions there will be 
A multitude of people with illnesses.
{{milestone:{label:20.45,id:UT22084-089-013-1789}}}“ ‘ “Although that land had fruits
That were large and sweet,
They will become bitter and hot,
And they will become small.
{{milestone:{label:20.46,id:UT22084-089-013-1790}}}“ ‘ “Games, amusements, and pleasures,
Those things that previously had been enjoyed,
Will be disliked and no longer pleasurable, 
And instead there will be dismay from hundreds of troubles.
{{milestone:{label:20.47,id:UT22084-089-013-3224}}}“ ‘ “The luster and the vitality
Of the harvests and fruits will perish,
And they will not bring satisfaction
To the body, the elements, or the senses.
{{milestone:{label:20.48,id:UT22084-089-013-1791}}}“ ‘ “Beings will have bad complexions, {{page:{number:197,id:UT22084-089-013-3148,folio:F.249.b}}}
Little strength, and will be emaciated.{{note:{index:422,id:UT22084-089-013-1792}}}
Even though they eat a lot of food,
They will not become satiated.
{{milestone:{label:20.49,id:UT22084-089-013-1793}}}“ ‘ “They will afterward cease to have
Strength, power, and diligence.
In that land, there will be
Beings with weak diligence.
{{milestone:{label:20.50,id:UT22084-089-013-1794}}}“ ‘ “There will be many sick beings
Afflicted by various diseases. 
There will planets and lunar asterisms
That arise from various rākṣasas.
{{milestone:{label:20.51,id:UT22084-089-013-1795}}}“ ‘ “The king who is not righteous,
Who is on the side of unrighteousness,
Will in the circle of the three worlds
Be destructive for the three realms.
{{milestone:{label:20.52,id:UT22084-089-013-1796}}}“ ‘ “When those on the side of the king
Who perform evil acts are left alone,
Then many of such evil actions
Will arise within those lands.
{{milestone:{label:20.53,id:UT22084-089-013-1797}}}“ ‘ “If the king ignores evil actions, 
He does not fulfill the purpose 
For which the lords of devas
Blessed him to become a king.
{{milestone:{label:20.54,id:UT22084-089-013-1798}}}“ ‘ “Through having done good actions,
Beings are reborn in the paradises.
Through doing bad actions, they are
Reborn as pretas, in hells, and as animals.
{{milestone:{label:20.55,id:UT22084-089-013-1799}}}“ ‘ “Whenever a king does nothing about
The wicked inhabitants in his realm,
Then through those evil acts being done,
Beings will fall from the Trāyastriṃśa paradise.
{{milestone:{label:20.56,id:UT22084-089-013-1800}}}“ ‘ “If he is not acting as a king,{{note:{index:423,id:UT22084-089-013-1801}}}
Then he will also not be a son,
And in the realm of his fathers, the deva kings,{{note:{index:424,id:UT22084-089-013-1802}}}
He will have become guilty of a crime.
{{milestone:{label:20.57,id:UT22084-089-013-1803}}}“ ‘ “When a kingdom is being destroyed
By extremely terrible dishonesty,
It is for that reason that the lords of devas
Blessed him to become a king in the human realm.
{{milestone:{label:20.58,id:UT22084-089-013-1804}}}“ ‘ “A king is someone who manifests
For beings the results of karma in that life.
He is someone who initiates good actions
In order to cause evil acts to cease,
And for the sake of Dharma in the land.{{note:{index:425,id:UT22084-089-013-1805}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.59,id:UT22084-089-013-1806}}}“ ‘ “Someone is called a king because their actions 
Are in order to teach the difference between
The results that ripen from the karma
Of having done good or having done bad.
{{milestone:{label:20.60,id:UT22084-089-013-1807}}}“ ‘ “He was blessed by the multitudes of devas 
For the benefit of himself and the benefit of others,
And for the benefit of the Dharma in that land, {{page:{number:198,id:UT22084-089-013-3149,folio:F.250.a}}}
And all those devas{{note:{index:426,id:UT22084-089-013-1808}}} are gladdened by him.
{{milestone:{label:20.61,id:UT22084-089-013-1809}}}“ ‘ “To subdue the deceitful, evil people 
Who are inhabitants in his domains,
And to benefit the Dharma in his kingdom,
He will give away his life and his kingship.
{{milestone:{label:20.62,id:UT22084-089-013-1810}}}“ ‘ “To accept unrighteousness
And to knowingly pay it no attention
Is a dreadful danger for the realm
With which nothing else can compare.
{{milestone:{label:20.63,id:UT22084-089-013-1811}}}“ ‘ “When there is the appearance of dishonesty,
If those who are dishonest are not punished,
Then afterward there will be in the land
Extremely dreadful dishonest people. 
{{milestone:{label:20.64,id:UT22084-089-013-1812}}}“ ‘ “They will destroy that kingdom
Like elephants do a great pond.
The lords of devas will also be disturbed,{{note:{index:427,id:UT22084-089-013-1813}}}
And it will bring ruin to the paradises.
{{milestone:{label:20.65,id:UT22084-089-013-1814}}}“ ‘ “Everything in the land
Will become pernicious.
Therefore, the evil actions of those who
Are wicked should be successively subdued.
{{milestone:{label:20.66,id:UT22084-089-013-1815}}}“ ‘ “He should protect the kingdom with righteousness
And he should never practice unrighteousness.
He should not become a sinful lord,{{note:{index:428,id:UT22084-089-013-1816}}}
Even if he has to give up his life.
{{milestone:{label:20.67,id:UT22084-089-013-1817}}}“ ‘ “Toward his family and other people,
Toward all the people in his kingdom,
The king should not show favoritism
Through which he will fall into bias.
{{milestone:{label:20.68,id:UT22084-089-013-1818}}}“ ‘ “The renown of a king who is 
Righteous will fill the three worlds,
And he will bring joy to the lords of devas
Who are in the Trāyastriṃśa paradise.
{{milestone:{label:20.69,id:UT22084-089-013-1819}}}“ ‘ “They will think, ‘Our son in Jambudvīpa 
Is in this way a righteous king.
He displays{{note:{index:429,id:UT22084-089-013-1820}}} a Dharma kingdom,
And establishes beings in good actions.’{{note:{index:430,id:UT22084-089-013-1821}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.70,id:UT22084-089-013-1822}}}“ ‘ “The king, through his good actions,
Inspires beings in this world to think
That the paradises are being filled
With devas and the children of devas. {{page:{number:199,id:UT22084-089-013-3150,folio:F.250.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.71,id:UT22084-089-013-1823}}}“ ‘ “Displaying there a Dharma kingdom
Will cause the kings to rejoice.
The lords of devas will favor{{note:{index:431,id:UT22084-089-013-1824}}} him,
And they will protect that human king.
{{milestone:{label:20.72,id:UT22084-089-013-1825}}}“ ‘ “The sun, the moon, and similarly
The lunar asterisms will move perfectly.
The winds will arise at the proper times,
And the rains will also come at the right time. 
{{milestone:{label:20.73,id:UT22084-089-013-1826}}}“ ‘ “There will be excellent harvests in the kingdom
And likewise in the realms of the devas.
The devas and the children of devas
Will fill the abodes of the devas.
{{milestone:{label:20.74,id:UT22084-089-013-1827}}}“ ‘ “In that way the monarch will
Give up his own dear life
In order to make the world happy
And not give up the precious Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:20.75,id:UT22084-089-013-1828}}}“ ‘ “The one who is adorned by good qualities
Relies on being in possession of righteousness.
He constantly makes beings happy,
And he constantly rejects bad actions.
{{milestone:{label:20.76,id:UT22084-089-013-1829}}}“ ‘ “He protects the realm with righteousness,
And he correctly teaches righteousness.
He establishes beings in good actions
And turns them away from bad actions.
{{milestone:{label:20.77,id:UT22084-089-013-1830}}}“ ‘ “When he correctly subjugates
Those who commit bad actions,
There will be good harvests in the kingdom,
And the king will have majesty.
{{milestone:{label:20.78,id:UT22084-089-013-1831}}} “ ‘ “The king will be renowned
And will protect the happiness of beings.” ’ ”
{{milestone:{label:20.79,id:UT22084-089-013-1832}}}This concludes “The King’s Treatise: The Commitment of the Lord of Devas,” the twentieth chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:21,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-21}}}Chapter 21: Susaṃbhava
{{milestone:{label:21.2,id:UT22084-089-013-1835}}}Then at that time, the Bhagavat recited these verses:
{{milestone:{label:21.3,id:UT22084-089-013-1836}}}“Whenever I was a cakravartin king,
I gave away the earth with its oceans.
I offered the four continents
Filled with jewels to the past jinas.
{{milestone:{label:21.4,id:UT22084-089-013-1837}}}“Because I sought the Dharma body,
There was nothing in the past that was pleasant 
And cherished that I did not give away,
And in many eons, I even gave up my cherished life.
{{milestone:{label:21.5,id:UT22084-089-013-1838}}}“Many countless eons ago,
I was King Susaṃbhava 
Within the teaching of the sugata Ratnaśikhin,
A sugata who had passed into nirvāṇa.
{{milestone:{label:21.6,id:UT22084-089-013-1839}}}“He was a cakravartin who ruled the four continents,
And he reigned{{note:{index:432,id:UT22084-089-013-1840}}} over the land as far as the oceans.
At that time, the excellent king went to sleep
In the royal palace for the teaching of the lord of jinas.
{{milestone:{label:21.7,id:UT22084-089-013-1841}}}“In a dream he heard the qualities of a buddha,
And in a dream{{note:{index:433,id:UT22084-089-013-1842}}} about the dharmabhāṇaka 
Ratnoccaya, he clearly saw him 
Teaching this lord of the sūtras.
{{milestone:{label:21.8,id:UT22084-089-013-1843}}}“That king awoke from his sleep, {{page:{number:200,id:UT22084-089-013-3151,folio:F.251.a}}}
His entire body filled with joy.
He reverently left the royal capital
And approached the excellent śrāvaka saṅgha. 
{{milestone:{label:21.9,id:UT22084-089-013-1844}}}“He made offerings to the Jina’s śrāvakas,
And he questioned this ārya saṅgha
About the dharmabhāṇaka Ratnoccaya:
‘Where is Ratnoccaya, the bhikṣu with qualities?’
{{milestone:{label:21.10,id:UT22084-089-013-1845}}}“At that time, Ratnoccaya
Was dwelling in another cave
In a state of happiness, contemplating
And reciting this king of sūtras.
{{milestone:{label:21.11,id:UT22084-089-013-1846}}}“Just then they showed the king
The dharmabhāṇaka Ratnoccaya,
Shining with perfect, glorious magnificence
And residing in another cave.
{{milestone:{label:21.12,id:UT22084-089-013-1847}}}“There the dharmabhāṇaka Ratnoccaya,
Who possessed the profound range of the jinas,{{note:{index:434,id:UT22084-089-013-1848}}}
Was constantly teaching the lord king of sūtras
That is called The Sublime Golden Light.
{{milestone:{label:21.13,id:UT22084-089-013-1849}}}“King Susaṃbhava bowed down 
To the feet of Ratnoccaya and said,
‘I pray to you, who has a face like the full moon, to teach 
The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.’
{{milestone:{label:21.14,id:UT22084-089-013-1850}}}“When Ratnoccaya promised that king,
Susaṃbhava, that he would do so,
All the devas throughout all the worlds
In the trichiliocosm became overjoyed. 
{{milestone:{label:21.15,id:UT22084-089-013-1851}}}“At that time, the lord of men sprinkled 
Precious water and scented water 
On the ground of a pure and superior place, 
Scattered flower petals, and arranged a throne.
{{milestone:{label:21.16,id:UT22084-089-013-1852}}}“The king adorned that throne with many thousands
Of parasols, banners, and rolls of silk.
The king scattered upon that throne
Various kinds of excellent sandalwood.
{{milestone:{label:21.17,id:UT22084-089-013-1853}}}“Devas, nāgas, asuras, kinnaras,
Yakṣa lords, yakṣas, and mahoragas
Rained down upon that throne
A shower of divine coral tree flowers.
{{milestone:{label:21.18,id:UT22084-089-013-1854}}}“Countless thousands of quintillions of devas 
Who longed for the Dharma arrived, {{page:{number:201,id:UT22084-089-013-3152,folio:F.251.b}}}
And they scattered sal{{note:{index:435,id:UT22084-089-013-1855}}} flowers
When Ratnoccaya was brought forth.
{{milestone:{label:21.19,id:UT22084-089-013-1856}}}“The dharmabhāṇaka Ratnoccaya
Washed his body and wore clean robes,
And when he approached that throne
With his palms together, he bowed to it. 
{{milestone:{label:21.20,id:UT22084-089-013-1857}}}“The deva lords, the devas and devīs
Residing in the sky, sent down a rain
Of coral tree flowers and played
Countless thousands of musical instruments.
{{milestone:{label:21.21,id:UT22084-089-013-1858}}}“The dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu Ratnoccaya,
Remembering countless thousands of millions 
Of buddhas in the ten directions,
Mounted the throne and sat upon it.
{{milestone:{label:21.22,id:UT22084-089-013-1859}}}“Thinking of all beings with kindness
And developing a compassionate mind,
At that time he taught this sūtra
To that king, Susaṃbhava.
{{milestone:{label:21.23,id:UT22084-089-013-1860}}}“The king bowed with palms together 
And rejoiced in each single word.
Through the Dharma’s power he shed tears,
And his body was permeated with joy.
{{milestone:{label:21.24,id:UT22084-089-013-1861}}}“In order to make an offering to this sūtra, 
At that time King Susaṃbhava held up
A king of precious wish-fulfilling jewels
And made a prayer for the benefit of all beings:
{{milestone:{label:21.25,id:UT22084-089-013-1862}}}“ ‘May there rain down on this Jambudvīpa
Jewelry that contain the seven jewels
And whatever great wealth{{note:{index:436,id:UT22084-089-013-1863}}} that will bring 
Happiness to the beings in this Jambudvīpa.’
{{milestone:{label:21.26,id:UT22084-089-013-1864}}}“Just then a rain of the seven jewels, 
Of armlets, necklaces, and excellent earrings, 
And similarly, food, drink, and clothing,{{note:{index:437,id:UT22084-089-013-1865}}}
Rained down upon the four continents.
{{milestone:{label:21.27,id:UT22084-089-013-1866}}}“When King Susaṃbhava saw
That precious rain fall on Jambudvīpa,
He offered the four continents that were
Filled with jewels to the teaching of Ratnaśikhin.{{note:{index:438,id:UT22084-089-013-1867}}}
{{milestone:{label:21.28,id:UT22084-089-013-1868}}}“I, the Tathāgata Śākyamuni, was
The king named Susaṃbhava, 
And at that time I offered up this earth
With its four continents filled with jewels.
{{milestone:{label:21.29,id:UT22084-089-013-1869}}}“The dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu Ratnoccaya,
Who was the one at that time who taught 
This sūtra to King Susaṃbhava, {{page:{number:202,id:UT22084-089-013-3153,folio:F.252.a}}}
Became the Tathāgata Akṣobhya.
{{milestone:{label:21.30,id:UT22084-089-013-1870}}}“Because of the good karma from
Listening at that time to this sūtra
And rejoicing in each single word,
Because of rejoicing and hearing the Dharma, 
{{milestone:{label:21.31,id:UT22084-089-013-1871}}}“I always have a body that is golden in color, 
Has the signs of a hundred merits,
Is beautiful to behold and a pleasure for the eyes,
And when seen gladdens ten billion devas and gladdens beings.
{{milestone:{label:21.32,id:UT22084-089-013-1872}}}“For ninety-nine trillion eons
I became a cakravartin king,
And for many hundreds of thousands of eons
I have experienced being the king of a realm.{{note:{index:439,id:UT22084-089-013-1873}}}
{{milestone:{label:21.33,id:UT22084-089-013-1874}}}“For countless eons I have been Śakras, and likewise 
I have been lords of Brahmās with peaceful{{note:{index:440,id:UT22084-089-013-1875}}} minds,
And I have pleased{{note:{index:441,id:UT22084-089-013-1876}}} countless ones with the ten strengths,
The number of which could never be known.
{{milestone:{label:21.34,id:UT22084-089-013-1877}}}“Through the immeasurable accumulation of abundant merit
From my hearing and rejoicing in this sūtra,
I attained the enlightenment that I had aspired to,
And I also attained the sublime Dharma body.”
{{milestone:{label:21.35,id:UT22084-089-013-1878}}}This concludes “Susaṃbhava,” the twenty-first chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:22,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-22}}}Chapter 22: The Protection Given by Yakṣas
{{milestone:{label:22.1,id:UT22084-089-013-1880}}}“Great goddess Śrī, any noble man or noble woman who has faith and wishes to make an inconceivably, extremely vast and great offering of requisites to the past, future, and present buddha bhagavats, and wishes to know the profound field of activity of the past, future, and present buddhas, whether in a temple or in a wilderness, in whatever place The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light is being correctly taught, in that place they should, with an undoubting and undistracted mind, pay attention and listen to this Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:22.2,id:UT22084-089-013-1881}}}Then the Bhagavat, in order to describe this extensively to the assembly, recited these verses: {{page:{number:203,id:UT22084-089-013-3154,folio:F.252.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.3,id:UT22084-089-013-1882}}}“Someone who wishes to make an 
Inconceivable offering to all the buddhas,
And wishes to know the profound
Field of activity of all the buddhas,
{{milestone:{label:22.4,id:UT22084-089-013-1883}}}“Should go to the place, whether
It is a temple or a dwelling, 
Where is taught this{{note:{index:442,id:UT22084-089-013-1884}}} sūtra of
The Sublime Golden Light.
{{milestone:{label:22.5,id:UT22084-089-013-1885}}}“This sūtra is inconceivable;
Its ocean of qualities is endless,
And it liberates all beings
From the oceans of many sufferings.{{note:{index:443,id:UT22084-089-013-1886}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.6,id:UT22084-089-013-1887}}}“I see the beginning of this sūtra
And also its middle and its conclusion.
This lord of sūtras is extremely profound.
There is no analogy that exists for it.
{{milestone:{label:22.7,id:UT22084-089-013-1888}}}“All of the particles that exist 
In the Ganges and on the earth, 
In the oceans and in the sky,
Cannot serve as an analogy for it.
{{milestone:{label:22.8,id:UT22084-089-013-1889}}}“The entrance to the Dharma realm 
Should be entered at that time.
Jina Śākyamuni should be seen 
In the center of a stūpa,
{{milestone:{label:22.9,id:UT22084-089-013-1890}}}“Which is the profound, enduring stūpa
That is the embodiment of the Dharma,
Teaching this sūtra perfectly
With a voice that is beautiful.
{{milestone:{label:22.10,id:UT22084-089-013-1891}}}“May the happiness of{{note:{index:444,id:UT22084-089-013-1892}}} devas 
And of humans be experienced 
For as many countless, innumerable
Million of eons as there are.
{{milestone:{label:22.11,id:UT22084-089-013-1893}}}“Whoever listens to this sūtra
Should think they will accomplish
My inconceivable accumulation of merit;
At that time, they should know this to be so.
{{milestone:{label:22.12,id:UT22084-089-013-1894}}}“Someone should, in order to listen to this sūtra,
Be able to endure the intense pain
Of crossing over a hundred-yojana-wide
Moat filled with a blazing inferno.
{{milestone:{label:22.13,id:UT22084-089-013-1895}}}“Then, as soon as they enter into
The temple or the dwelling,
Their bad karma will be eliminated
And all the qualities of nightmares,
{{milestone:{label:22.14,id:UT22084-089-013-1896}}}Harm from planets and lunar asterisms,
And terrible evil spirits and demons
Will be entirely driven away
The moment that they enter there.
{{milestone:{label:22.15,id:UT22084-089-013-1897}}}“There the Dharmabhāṇaka should make a seat
That is in the form of a lotus
Exactly as has been revealed
By nāga kings in a dream.{{note:{index:445,id:UT22084-089-013-1898}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.16,id:UT22084-089-013-1899}}}“Having sat upon that seat,
They should teach this sūtra,
Write it out, and read it out loud, {{page:{number:204,id:UT22084-089-013-3155,folio:F.253.a}}}
And similarly, they should learn it.
{{milestone:{label:22.17,id:UT22084-089-013-1900}}}“After they have risen from that seat,
Even if they go to another land,
Miraculous manifestations 
Will appear on that seat.
{{milestone:{label:22.18,id:UT22084-089-013-1901}}}“Sometimes the form of the
Dharmabhāṇaka will appear there, 
And sometimes the form of a buddha,
Sometimes that of a bodhisattva,
{{milestone:{label:22.19,id:UT22084-089-013-1902}}}“Sometimes that of Samantabhadra,
Sometimes that of Mañjuśrī,
And sometimes that of Maitreya
Will appear upon that seat.
{{milestone:{label:22.20,id:UT22084-089-013-1903}}}“Sometimes only light will appear.
Sometimes devas will appear—
They will appear there briefly,
And then they will disappear.
{{milestone:{label:22.21,id:UT22084-089-013-1904}}}“If a buddha is seen, there will be praise.{{note:{index:446,id:UT22084-089-013-1905}}}
Everything will be accomplished.
There will be perfect opulence{{note:{index:447,id:UT22084-089-013-1906}}} and good fortune.
This is an omen emanated by the Buddha.{{note:{index:448,id:UT22084-089-013-1907}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.22,id:UT22084-089-013-1908}}}“There will be victory and glory and fame.
Those who are adversaries will be repulsed.
The opposing armies of enemies will defeated.
Enemies will be vanquished in battle.
{{milestone:{label:22.23,id:UT22084-089-013-1909}}}“All nightmares will come to an end.
All bad actions will be eliminated;
All bad actions will be brought to an end.
There will be victory in battle.{{note:{index:449,id:UT22084-089-013-1910}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.24,id:UT22084-089-013-1911}}}“One will have fame that will spread
Throughout the entirety of this Jambudvīpa.
All the enemies that he has
Will be completely defeated.
{{milestone:{label:22.25,id:UT22084-089-013-1912}}}“Enemies will constantly be vanquished. 
All bad actions will be abandoned.
There will be victory in battle,
Freedom from enemies, and perfect joy.
{{milestone:{label:22.26,id:UT22084-089-013-1913}}}“The Lord of Brahmās, the Lord of Trāyastriṃśa,
And similarly the guardians of the world;
Vajrapāṇi who is the lord of yakṣas;
Saṃjñeya, the supreme victorious leader;
{{milestone:{label:22.27,id:UT22084-089-013-1914}}}“The lord of nāgas, Anavatapta;
And likewise Sāgara,
The lord of kinnaras and lord of asuras;
And also the lord of the garuḍas—
{{milestone:{label:22.28,id:UT22084-089-013-1915}}}“Those and also all such others,
Every one of all of the devas—
Will constantly make offerings to
The inconceivable stūpa of the Dharma,
And they will feel great joy on seeing
Beings who have reverence. {{page:{number:205,id:UT22084-089-013-3156,folio:F.253.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.29,id:UT22084-089-013-1916}}}“The supreme lords of the devas
Will all in their minds be thinking, 
And every one of the devas 
Will be saying to one another,
{{milestone:{label:22.30,id:UT22084-089-013-1917}}}“ ‘Look at them, they who have 
Accumulated merit, glory, and majesty!
They have come here{{note:{index:450,id:UT22084-089-013-1918}}}
To listen to this profound sūtra.
{{milestone:{label:22.31,id:UT22084-089-013-1919}}}“ ‘Those humans who have arrived here 
Through having developed good roots{{note:{index:451,id:UT22084-089-013-1920}}}
Have reverence for the stūpa of the Dharma,
With a faith that is inconceivable.
{{milestone:{label:22.32,id:UT22084-089-013-1921}}}“ ‘They have compassion for the world
And they bring benefit to beings.
They are vessels for the flavor of the sublime Dharma 
That comes from the profound Dharmas.
{{milestone:{label:22.33,id:UT22084-089-013-1922}}}“ ‘They have entered through
The entrance to the Dharma realm.
They who listen to this sublime goodness,
The Sūtra of the Sublime Golden Light,
{{milestone:{label:22.34,id:UT22084-089-013-1923}}}“ ‘Have in the past made offerings
To a hundred thousand buddhas;
It is because of those good roots
That they are listening to the sūtra.’
{{milestone:{label:22.35,id:UT22084-089-013-1924}}}“All the lords and kings of devas—
Sarasvatī, and similarly
Śrī and Vaiśravaṇa,
And, similarly, the Four Mahārājas,{{note:{index:452,id:UT22084-089-013-1925}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.36,id:UT22084-089-013-1926}}}“And the hundred thousand yakṣas
Who have great might and miraculous powers—
All of them in the four directions{{note:{index:453,id:UT22084-089-013-1927}}}
Will give them perfect protection.
{{milestone:{label:22.37,id:UT22084-089-013-1928}}}“Indra, Soma, and Yama,
Vāyu and Varuṇa, 
Skanda, Viṣṇu, Sarasvatī, 
Consumer of Burnt Offerings, and Prajāpati,{{note:{index:454,id:UT22084-089-013-1929}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.38,id:UT22084-089-013-1930}}}“Those who with great power subjugate adversaries,
All those protectors of the world,
Day and night, never inattentive,
Will give them their protection.{{note:{index:455,id:UT22084-089-013-1931}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.39,id:UT22084-089-013-1932}}}“The yakṣa lords that have great might{{note:{index:456,id:UT22084-089-013-1933}}}—
Nārāyaṇa and Maheśvara,
Saṃjñeya, and also the rest of
The other twenty-eight yakṣas,{{note:{index:457,id:UT22084-089-013-1934}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.40,id:UT22084-089-013-1935}}}“And the hundred thousand yakṣas
With their great might and miraculous powers—
Will give them their protection
From all terror and fears.
{{milestone:{label:22.41,id:UT22084-089-013-1936}}}“Vajrapāṇi, the lord of yakṣas, 
With five hundred yakṣas
And all the bodhisattvas,
Will give them his protection.
{{milestone:{label:22.42,id:UT22084-089-013-1937}}}“Maṇibhadra, the lord of yakṣas, {{page:{number:206,id:UT22084-089-013-3157,folio:F.254.a}}}
And similarly, Pūrṇabhadra, 
Kumbhīra and Aṭavika, 
Piṅgala and Kapila—
{{milestone:{label:22.43,id:UT22084-089-013-1938}}}“Each of those lords of yakṣas,
Accompanied by five hundred yakṣas—
Will give their protection to
Those who listen to this sūtra. 
{{milestone:{label:22.44,id:UT22084-089-013-1939}}}“Gandharva and Citrasena,
Jinarāja and Jinarṣabha,
Maṇikaṇṭha and Nikaṇṭha,
And similarly Varṣādhipati; 
{{milestone:{label:22.45,id:UT22084-089-013-1940}}}“Mahāgrāsa and Mahākāla,{{note:{index:458,id:UT22084-089-013-1941}}}
And similarly also Svarṇakeśin, 
Pāñcika, and Chagalapāda, 
And similarly also Mahābhāga;
{{milestone:{label:22.46,id:UT22084-089-013-1942}}}“Praṇālin and Mahāpāla, 
Markaṭa and also Vāli,
Sūciroma and Sūryamitra,{{note:{index:459,id:UT22084-089-013-1943}}}
And similarly Ratnakeśa; 
{{milestone:{label:22.47,id:UT22084-089-013-1944}}}“Mahāpraṇālin and Nakula,
Kāmaśreṣṭha and Candana,

And similarly Sātāgiri—
{{milestone:{label:22.48,id:UT22084-089-013-1946}}}“All of them, who have great might,
Subjugate adversaries, and have miraculous power—
Will give their protection to
Those who listen to this sūtra. 
{{milestone:{label:22.49,id:UT22084-089-013-1947}}}“The nāga lord Anavatapta, 
And similarly Sāgara,
Both Elapatra and Mucilinda, 
And Nanda and Upananda,
{{milestone:{label:22.50,id:UT22084-089-013-1948}}}“With a hundred thousand nāgas

From all terrors and fears.
{{milestone:{label:22.51,id:UT22084-089-013-1949}}}“Bali, Rāhu, and Namuci,

Prahrāda and Kharaskandha,

{{milestone:{label:22.52,id:UT22084-089-013-1950}}}“With a hundred thousand asuras
With great might and miraculous powers, 
Will give them their protection
From all terrors and fears.
{{milestone:{label:22.53,id:UT22084-089-013-1951}}}“Hārītī, the mother of spirits,
With her five hundred children, 
Will give them their protection
While they sit, sleep, or are intoxicated.{{note:{index:461,id:UT22084-089-013-1952}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.54,id:UT22084-089-013-1953}}}“Caṇḍā and Caṇḍālikā, 
And similarly the yakṣiṇī Caṇḍikā, 
Conch Shell,{{note:{index:462,id:UT22084-089-013-1954}}} and Kūṭadantī, 
And also Yakṣiṇī Thief of All Beings’ Splendor{{note:{index:463,id:UT22084-089-013-1955}}}— 
{{milestone:{label:22.55,id:UT22084-089-013-1956}}}“All of them, who have great might,
Subjugate adversaries, and have miraculous power—
Will give their protection to them
Everywhere in the four directions. {{page:{number:207,id:UT22084-089-013-3158,folio:F.254.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.56,id:UT22084-089-013-1957}}}“Sarasvatī and all the other
Countless numbers of goddesses,
And similarly Śrī and 
All of the other goddesses—
{{milestone:{label:22.57,id:UT22084-089-013-1958}}}“The goddess of the earth and
The goddesses of harvests, fruits, and forests;
Those who dwell in parks, trees, and caityas; 
And the goddesses of the wind—
{{milestone:{label:22.58,id:UT22084-089-013-1959}}}“Every one of those goddesses, 
With their minds filled with joy,
Will here give their protection
To those who delight in this sūtra.
{{milestone:{label:22.59,id:UT22084-089-013-1960}}}“They will bestow on those beings
Life and color and strength,
And will constantly adorn them with perfect
Glory and merit and magnificence. 
{{milestone:{label:22.60,id:UT22084-089-013-1961}}}“They will end all harm from 
The planets and the lunar asterisms.
They will bring to an end all troubles,
Bad actions, and nightmares.
{{milestone:{label:22.61,id:UT22084-089-013-1962}}}“The goddess of the earth herself, 
Who has depth and great strength,
Will be satiated by the flavor of 
The Lord King of Sūtras, The Sublime Golden Light.
{{milestone:{label:22.62,id:UT22084-089-013-1963}}}“For sixty-eight thousand
Times a hundred yojanas,
As far down as the vajra foundation,
The fertility of the earth will increase.
{{milestone:{label:22.63,id:UT22084-089-013-1964}}}“The fertility of the earth that has sunk
A whole hundred yojanas below
Will rise back upward
And enrich the surfaces.
{{milestone:{label:22.64,id:UT22084-089-013-1965}}}“Every one of all those devas, through
The power of listening to the sūtra,
Will be satiated by the flavor of 
The Lord King of Sūtras, The Sublime Golden Light.
{{milestone:{label:22.65,id:UT22084-089-013-1966}}}“They will become perfectly brilliant,{{note:{index:464,id:UT22084-089-013-1967}}}
And similarly they will have strength.
They will be happy and satisfied.
Throughout the entirety of Jambudvīpa,{{note:{index:465,id:UT22084-089-013-1968}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.66,id:UT22084-089-013-1969}}}“The devas of fruits, harvests, and forests
Will be satisfied by various flavors,
And they will be completely delighted,
Satisfied by the flavor of the sūtra.
{{milestone:{label:22.67,id:UT22084-089-013-1970}}}“Then the fruits and the harvests,
And the various kinds of flowers 
And the various kinds of fruit trees,
Will all develop perfectly.
{{milestone:{label:22.68,id:UT22084-089-013-1971}}}“All the fruit trees,
The parks, and the forests
Will blossom with flowers
Emitting their various aromas. {{page:{number:208,id:UT22084-089-013-3159,folio:F.255.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.69,id:UT22084-089-013-1972}}}“All the plants and trees
That have various kinds of flowers
And various kinds of fruits
Will grow upon the earth.
{{milestone:{label:22.70,id:UT22084-089-013-1973}}}“Throughout the entirety of this Jambudvīpa
There will be innumerable nāga maidens
Whose minds will become filled with joy,
And they will come to where the ponds are.
{{milestone:{label:22.71,id:UT22084-089-013-1974}}}“And there will grow in all the ponds 
A variety of night lotuses, 
Red lotuses, and similarly 
Blue lotuses and white lotuses. 
{{milestone:{label:22.72,id:UT22084-089-013-3225}}}“In the sky there will be no smoke,
And it will not be covered by clouds.
There will be no darkness and no dust,
And everywhere will be completely bright.
{{milestone:{label:22.73,id:UT22084-089-013-1975}}}“A bright and beautiful{{note:{index:466,id:UT22084-089-013-1976}}} net of light rays
That has a thousand rays of sunlight
Brings the most perfect joy
With its profound brightness.
{{milestone:{label:22.74,id:UT22084-089-013-1977}}}“Even that lord, the deva Sūrya, 
Dwelling in his divine palace
Made of Jambū River{{note:{index:467,id:UT22084-089-013-1978}}} gold,
Will gain satisfaction through this sūtra.
{{milestone:{label:22.75,id:UT22084-089-013-1979}}}“When Lord Sūrya is gladdened,
He will shine onto Jambudvīpa;
He will completely illuminate it
With an infinite net of light rays.
{{milestone:{label:22.76,id:UT22084-089-013-1980}}}“Simply through his rising,
He will shine a net of light rays,
And the lotuses that fill
A variety of ponds will open.
{{milestone:{label:22.77,id:UT22084-089-013-1981}}}“Throughout the entirety of this Jambudvīpa,
The various flowers, fruits, and herbs
Will perfectly, completely ripen,
And the entire earth will be satisfied.{{note:{index:468,id:UT22084-089-013-1982}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.78,id:UT22084-089-013-1983}}}“The moon and the sun also 
Will at that time be brighter.
The lunar asterisms will move perfectly,
And similarly so will the winds.
{{milestone:{label:22.79,id:UT22084-089-013-1984}}}“Throughout all of Jambudvīpa
There will be excellent harvests.
Wherever this sūtra is present,
That kingdom will be preeminent.”
{{milestone:{label:22.80,id:UT22084-089-013-1985}}}This concludes “The Protection Given by Yakṣas,” the twenty-second chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:23,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-23}}}Chapter 23: The Prophecy to Ten Thousand Devas
{{milestone:{label:23.1,id:UT22084-089-013-1987}}}When the Bhagavat had said that, the noble goddess Bodhisattvasamuccayā{{note:{index:469,id:UT22084-089-013-1988}}} asked him, “Venerable Bhagavat, {{page:{number:209,id:UT22084-089-013-3160,folio:F.255.b}}} through what cause and what condition, and through what accomplishment and accumulation of planting good roots, have Jvalanāntara­tejo­rāja and these other ten thousand devas now come from the Trāyastriṃśa paradise, having heard the prophecy to these three sublime beings?
{{milestone:{label:23.2,id:UT22084-089-013-1989}}}“It was thus: this excellent being, the bodhisattva Ruciraketu, in a future time, after many hundreds of thousands of quintillions of asaṃkhyeyas of eons have passed, will attain the highest, most complete enlightenment of buddhahood in the world realm Suvarṇaprabhā. He will appear in that world as the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha, the one with wisdom and virtuous conduct,{{note:{index:470,id:UT22084-089-013-1990}}} the sugata, the one who knows the world’s beings, the unsurpassable guide who tames beings, the teacher of devas and humans, the buddha, the bhagavat by the name of Suvarṇa­ratnākaracchatra­kūṭa.
{{milestone:{label:23.3,id:UT22084-089-013-1991}}}“When the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha Suvarṇa­ratnākaracchatra­kūṭa has passed into nirvāṇa and his Dharma has come to an end and his teachings have completely come to an end, at that time, this boy by the name of Rūpyaketu{{note:{index:471,id:UT22084-089-013-1992}}} will appear as the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha by the name of Suvarṇa­jambu­dhvaja­kāñcanābha in the world realm called Virajadhvajā. {{page:{number:210,id:UT22084-089-013-3161,folio:F.256.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:23.4,id:UT22084-089-013-1993}}}“When the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha Suvarṇa­jambu­dhvaja­kāñcanābha has passed into nirvāṇa and his Dharma has come to an end and his teachings have completely come to an end, then this boy, by the name of Rūpyaprabha, will be the successor of that tathāgata, attaining the highest enlightenment of complete buddhahood in the world realm called Immaculate Banner, appearing as the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha, the one with wisdom and virtuous conduct, the sugata, the one who knows the world’s beings, the unsurpassable guide who tames beings, the teacher of devas and humans, the buddha, the bhagavat by the name of Essence of the Radiance of a Hundred Golden Lights. 
{{milestone:{label:23.5,id:UT22084-089-013-1994}}}“All of that was the Bhagavat’s prophecy of their attainment of the highest, most complete enlightenment.”
{{milestone:{label:23.6,id:UT22084-089-013-1995}}}Then the noble goddess Bodhisattvasamuccayā said to the Bhagavat,{{note:{index:472,id:UT22084-089-013-1996}}} “Venerable Bhagavat, Jvalanāntara­tejo­rāja and the rest of those ten thousand devas have not had such a great, extensive bodhisattva conduct as that. 
{{milestone:{label:23.7,id:UT22084-089-013-1997}}}“It is not said that they have previously practiced the six perfections. 
{{milestone:{label:23.8,id:UT22084-089-013-1998}}}“It is not said that they have previously given away their arms, legs, eyes, the supreme limb of the head, or their beloved sons, wives, and daughters. 
{{milestone:{label:23.9,id:UT22084-089-013-1999}}}“It is not said that they have previously given away wealth, grain, cowries, gold, silver, jewels, pearls, beryl, conchs, crystals, coral, silver, or gold nuggets. 
{{milestone:{label:23.10,id:UT22084-089-013-2000}}}“It is not said that they have previously given away food, drink, steeds, clothes, beds, seats,{{note:{index:473,id:UT22084-089-013-2001}}} houses, divine palaces, parks, ponds, or pools.
{{milestone:{label:23.11,id:UT22084-089-013-2002}}}“It is not said that they have previously given away elephants, oxen, stallions, male servants, or female servants.
{{milestone:{label:23.12,id:UT22084-089-013-2003}}}“Countless hundreds of thousands of quintillions of bodhisattvas have, before they received from buddha bhagavats their names as tathāgatas, made countless hundreds of thousands of various offerings and all requisites{{note:{index:474,id:UT22084-089-013-2004}}} to countless hundreds of thousands of quintillions of tathāgatas for countless hundreds of thousands of quintillions of eons. {{page:{number:211,id:UT22084-089-013-3162,folio:F.256.b}}} They had given away all the things that could be given away. They had given away their arms, legs, eyes, the supreme limb of the head, and their beloved sons, wives, and daughters. They had given away wealth, grain, cowries, gold, silver, jewels, pearls, beryl, conchs, crystals, coral, silver, and gold nuggets. They had given away food, drink, steeds, clothes, beds, seats, houses, divine palaces, parks, pleasure groves,{{note:{index:475,id:UT22084-089-013-2005}}} ponds, pools, elephants, oxen, stallions, male servants, and female servants. They had successively completed all the six perfections and, having successively completed all the six perfections, they experienced many hundreds of thousands of kinds of happiness.
{{milestone:{label:23.13,id:UT22084-089-013-2006}}}“Venerable Bhagavat, through what cause and what condition, through what manner of developing good roots, have Jvalanāntara­tejo­rāja and the rest of these ten thousand devas who have come here to hear the Dharma from the Bhagavat been prophesied to successively appear, Bhagavat, in a future time, after many hundreds of thousands of quintillions of asaṃkhyeya eons, in a world realm called Śālendra­dhvajāgravatī, in the same family, in the same clan, and with the same name to attain the highest, most complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, as ten thousand buddhas by the name of Prasanna­vadanotpala­gandha­kūṭa, {{page:{number:212,id:UT22084-089-013-3163,folio:F.257.a}}} becoming tathāgatas, arhats, samyaksaṃbuddhas, with wisdom and virtuous conduct, sugatas, knowers of the world’s beings, unsurpassable guides who tame beings, teachers of devas and humans, buddhas, and bhagavats?”
{{milestone:{label:23.14,id:UT22084-089-013-2007}}}When she had asked that, the Bhagavat said, “Noble goddess, Jvalanāntara­tejo­rāja and the rest of these ten thousand devas do have a development of good roots, do have a cause, and do have deeds that they have accomplished and accumulated, through which they have come here from the paradise of Trāyastriṃśa in order to hear the Dharma. 
{{milestone:{label:23.15,id:UT22084-089-013-2008}}}“Noble goddess, when they heard the prophecy of the enlightenment of these three excellent beings, as soon as they heard it, they gained reverence{{note:{index:476,id:UT22084-089-013-2009}}} for, delight in, and trust in this Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light, and just through that they had minds that were as completely pure as stainless beryl. They had profound, completely clear minds like pure, extremely vast, and expansive space. They possessed an immeasurable accumulation of merit.
{{milestone:{label:23.16,id:UT22084-089-013-2010}}}“Noble goddess, Jvalanāntara­tejo­rāja and the rest of these ten thousand devas, in just that way, as soon as they heard this king that is The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light, gained reverence for and trust in it. In just that way, they had minds that were as completely pure as stainless beryl, and therefore they attained the level of prophecy.
{{milestone:{label:23.17,id:UT22084-089-013-2011}}}“Noble goddess, it is through this accumulation of good roots and through the power of previous prayers that Jvalanāntara­tejo­rāja and the rest of these ten thousand devas have now obtained the prophecy of their highest, most complete enlightenment.”
{{milestone:{label:23.18,id:UT22084-089-013-2012}}}This concludes “The Prophecy to Ten Thousand Devas,” the twenty-third chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.” {{page:{number:213,id:UT22084-089-013-3164,folio:F.257.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:24,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-24}}}Chapter 24: Ending All Illness
{{milestone:{label:24.1,id:UT22084-089-013-2014}}}“Noble goddess, what were those past prayers? In the past, in a time gone by—an inconceivable, vast number, more innumerable than an asaṃkhyeya of eons ago—at that time, in that time, the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha, the one with wisdom and virtuous conduct, the sugata, the one who knows the world’s beings, the unsurpassable guide who tames beings, the teacher of devas and humans, the buddha, the bhagavat by the name of Ratnaśikhin appeared in the world. 
{{milestone:{label:24.2,id:UT22084-089-013-2015}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, after the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha Ratnaśikhin had passed into nirvāṇa and the Dharma had vanished and there was just the outer appearance of the Dharma, there was King Sureśvaraprabha, who followed the Dharma, who was a Dharma king, who ruled the kingdom through the Dharma and not through that which was not the Dharma, and who was like a father and mother to the beings who dwelled there.
{{milestone:{label:24.3,id:UT22084-089-013-2016}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, in the kingdom of King Sureśvaraprabha, there was a head merchant by the name of Jaṭiṃdhara. He was a doctor, a physician, perfectly skilled in the humors, and was endowed with all eight branches of the Āyurveda tradition.
{{milestone:{label:24.4,id:UT22084-089-013-2017}}}“O noble goddess, at that time, in that time, the head merchant Jaṭiṃdhara had a son named Jalavāhana, who had an excellent body; was attractive and handsome; had a perfect, well-developed, excellent complexion; was learned in various treatises; had the understanding of all treatises; and was perfectly trained in letters, numbers, finger-counting, and calculations.
{{milestone:{label:24.5,id:UT22084-089-013-2018}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, {{page:{number:214,id:UT22084-089-013-3165,folio:F.258.a}}} many hundreds of thousands of beings living in the kingdom of King Sureśvaraprabha were afflicted by various illnesses, tormented by various illnesses, and were experiencing severe, terrible, unendurable, unpleasant sensations of suffering. 
{{milestone:{label:24.6,id:UT22084-089-013-2019}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, there arose in Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, great compassion for those many hundreds of thousands of beings who were afflicted by various illnesses and tormented by various illnesses. He thought, ‘Those beings are experiencing severe, terrible, unendurable, unpleasant sensations of suffering, and my father, this head merchant Jaṭiṃdhara, who is a doctor, a physician, perfectly skilled in the humors, and endowed with all eight branches of the Āyurveda tradition, has become old, decrepit, and feeble. He has reached an advanced age, walks leaning on a stick, and is unable to go to the villages, the towns, the market towns, the countryside, the realm, or the royal capital. Therefore, in order to free those many hundreds of thousands of beings from the afflictions of various illnesses and the torments of various illnesses, I will go to my father, Jaṭiṃdhara, and question him so as to become skilled in the humors in order to heal illness. Having questioned him so as to become skilled in the humors, I will go to the villages, towns, market towns, countryside, realm, and royal capital. When I go there, I will free the many hundreds of thousands of beings from illness.’
{{milestone:{label:24.7,id:UT22084-089-013-2020}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, went to his father, Jaṭiṃdhara, and having come to him, he bowed down his head in homage at his father’s feet, and with his palms together he sat to one side. When he had seated himself to one side, {{page:{number:215,id:UT22084-089-013-3166,folio:F.258.b}}} Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, recited these verses to his father, Jaṭiṃdhara, questioning him about skill in the humors:
{{milestone:{label:24.8,id:UT22084-089-013-2021}}}“ ‘How are physical powers destroyed{{note:{index:477,id:UT22084-089-013-2022}}}
And how do the humors change?
At what times do illnesses
Arise within physical beings?
{{milestone:{label:24.9,id:UT22084-089-013-2023}}}“ ‘What foods should be eaten or not
At different times for health,
So that within someone’s body
The body’s heat{{note:{index:478,id:UT22084-089-013-2024}}} will not be harmed?
{{milestone:{label:24.10,id:UT22084-089-013-2025}}}“ ‘What are the medical practices
For healing the illnesses
That arise from air, from bile,
From phlegm, and from their combination?
{{milestone:{label:24.11,id:UT22084-089-013-2026}}}“ ‘During which times does the air move,
During which times does the bile move,
And during which times does the phlegm move,
Through which there will be harm to humans?’
{{milestone:{label:24.12,id:UT22084-089-013-2027}}}“Then the head merchant, Jaṭiṃdhara, taught his son Jalavāhana skill in the humors by reciting these verses:
{{milestone:{label:24.13,id:UT22084-089-013-2028}}}“ ‘Know three months to be summer and three months the autumn,
And there are three that are winter and three that are spring.
Similarly, there are said to be six seasons,{{note:{index:479,id:UT22084-089-013-2029}}}
And there are twelve months in one year. 
{{milestone:{label:24.14,id:UT22084-089-013-2030}}}“ ‘Know that the months are divided into threes,
And that pairs of months are taught.
Food and drink are digested accordingly.
Thus the physicians teach humors and time.
{{milestone:{label:24.15,id:UT22084-089-013-2031}}}“ ‘The faculties and the humors
Are in groups within each year.
It is when the faculties transform
That various illnesses arise in beings
{{milestone:{label:24.16,id:UT22084-089-013-2032}}}“ ‘Know that the physician must be skilled
In the groups of three and four months,
The six times and the six humors,
And the food, drink, and medicines that correspond.
{{milestone:{label:24.17,id:UT22084-089-013-2033}}}“ ‘Illness that is primarily air arises in the summer.{{note:{index:480,id:UT22084-089-013-2034}}}
That which arises in the autumn is the movement of bile.
Similarly, during the time of winter it is the aggregation,
And illness that is primarily phlegm arises in spring.{{note:{index:481,id:UT22084-089-013-2035}}}
{{milestone:{label:24.18,id:UT22084-089-013-2036}}}“ ‘In summer: oily, pungent, salty, and sour tastes;
In autumn: the sweet, the oily, and the cool;
In winter: the sweet, the oily, and the sour;
And in the time of spring, the astringent, pungent, and bitter.{{note:{index:482,id:UT22084-089-013-2037}}}{{page:{number:216,id:UT22084-089-013-3167,folio:F.259.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:24.19,id:UT22084-089-013-2038}}}“ ‘That which is primarily phlegm arises immediately after eating.
That which is primarily bile arises during digestion.
That which is primarily air arises immediately after digestion.
That which is the movement of all three humors is like that.
{{milestone:{label:24.20,id:UT22084-089-013-2039}}}“ ‘That which has the nature of air is healed by nutrition.
Laxative medicines are what dispel bile illness.
Aggregate illnesses will accord with all three.
For the class of phlegm, give emetic medicines.
{{milestone:{label:24.21,id:UT22084-089-013-2040}}}“ ‘Know the groups that are primarily 
Air, bile, aggregation, or phlegm.
Rely upon the medicines, food, and drink
For whichever time, humor, and body.’
{{milestone:{label:24.22,id:UT22084-089-013-2041}}}“Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, through just this inquiry into skill in the humors became learned in all the eight branches of the Āyurveda. 
{{milestone:{label:24.23,id:UT22084-089-013-2042}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son went throughout all the villages, towns, market towns, countryside, realm, and the royal capital in the kingdom of King Sureśvaraprabha, and he said, ‘I will be a doctor for you many hundreds of thousands of beings who are afflicted by various illnesses and tormented by various illnesses. I promise to be your doctor and I will free you from your various illnesses and bring you relief.’
{{milestone:{label:24.24,id:UT22084-089-013-2043}}}“Noble goddess, when all those many hundreds of thousands of beings heard those words spoken by Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, they immediately felt great joy. They found relief and had inconceivable joy, happiness, and delight.
{{milestone:{label:24.25,id:UT22084-089-013-2044}}}“At that time, in that time, those many hundreds of thousands of beings who were afflicted by various illnesses and tormented by various illnesses were completely freed from their illness and became healthy. When they became healthy, they had the same power, strength and vigor as before.
{{milestone:{label:24.26,id:UT22084-089-013-2045}}}“At that time, in that time, all those who were afflicted with severe illnesses among the many hundreds of thousands of beings that were afflicted by various illnesses and tormented by various illnesses {{page:{number:217,id:UT22084-089-013-3168,folio:F.259.b}}} went to Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, and Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, cured all those beings of all their illnesses by using whatever medical treatments he had given the many hundreds of thousands of beings that were afflicted by various illnesses and tormented by various illnesses. They became free of illness, or their illness was diminished and they became healthy, and they had the same power, strength, and vigor as before.
{{milestone:{label:24.27,id:UT22084-089-013-2046}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, in that time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, freed from their various illnesses the many hundreds of thousands of beings who were afflicted by various illnesses and tormented by various illnesses throughout all the villages, towns, market towns, countryside, realm, and the royal capital in the kingdom of King Sureśvaraprabha.” 
{{milestone:{label:24.28,id:UT22084-089-013-2047}}}This concludes “Ending All Illness,” the twenty-fourth chapter of “The Lord King of Sūtras, the Sublime Golden Light.”
{{milestone:{label:25,id:UT22084-089-013-chapter-25}}}Chapter 25: The Story of the Fish Guided by Jalavāhana
{{milestone:{label:25.1,id:UT22084-089-013-2049}}}“And so, noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, had cured the illnesses in the kingdom of King Sureśvaraprabha, so that there were few illnesses and people had the enthusiasm and physical strength they had previously possessed. All the beings in the kingdom of King Sureśvaraprabha were happy, enjoyed amusements, performed acts of generosity, and created merit. They praised Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, saying, ‘May Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, be victorious! May he be victorious! He is the king of healing,{{note:{index:483,id:UT22084-089-013-2050}}} who heals the illnesses of all beings. He is the visible presence of a bodhisattva, and he knows all the eight branches of the Āyurveda.’
{{milestone:{label:25.2,id:UT22084-089-013-2051}}}“Noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, had a wife by the name of Jalāmbujagarbhā. {{page:{number:218,id:UT22084-089-013-3169,folio:F.260.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:25.3,id:UT22084-089-013-2052}}}“Noble goddess, the wife, Jalāmbujagarbhā, had two sons. The name of one was Jalāmbara and the name of the other was Jalagarbha. 
{{milestone:{label:25.4,id:UT22084-089-013-2053}}}“Noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, traveled with his two sons successively through the villages, towns, market towns, countryside, realm, and the royal capital.
{{milestone:{label:25.5,id:UT22084-089-013-2054}}}“Noble goddess, at another time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, went into an empty{{note:{index:484,id:UT22084-089-013-2055}}} wilderness. In that empty{{note:{index:485,id:UT22084-089-013-2056}}} wilderness he saw carnivores—dogs, jackals, crows, and other birds—that were hurrying toward a lake in that wilderness, and he wondered, ‘Why are these carnivores—dogs, jackals, and so on, up to birds—hurrying in that direction?’ Then he also thought, ‘I will go in the direction that the dogs, jackals, crows, and other birds are rushing.’
{{milestone:{label:25.6,id:UT22084-089-013-2057}}}“Noble goddess, then Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, went along in that way until he eventually came to the lake in the empty{{note:{index:486,id:UT22084-089-013-2058}}} wilderness where they were going. Ten thousand fish lived in that great lake. He saw that many hundreds of the fish had no water and he felt great compassion for them. Then he saw emerging from a tree the upper half of the body of a goddess. The goddess said to Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, ‘Excellent, noble son, excellent. Why is that? Because your name is Jalavāhana you must give water to these fish. You are called Jalavāhana for two reasons, because you bring water and because you give water.{{note:{index:487,id:UT22084-089-013-2059}}} Therefore act in accordance with your name!’
{{milestone:{label:25.7,id:UT22084-089-013-2060}}}“Jalavāhana asked the goddess, ‘Goddess, how many of these fish are there?’
{{milestone:{label:25.8,id:UT22084-089-013-2061}}}“The goddess replied, ‘A full ten thousand fish.’
{{milestone:{label:25.9,id:UT22084-089-013-2062}}}“Then, noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, developed an even greater motivation of compassion.
{{milestone:{label:25.10,id:UT22084-089-013-2063}}}“Noble goddess, at that time, there was just a little water left in that great lake in the empty{{note:{index:488,id:UT22084-089-013-2064}}} wilderness, {{page:{number:219,id:UT22084-089-013-3170,folio:F.260.b}}} and those ten thousand fish were close to death, deprived of water, and rushing and darting around.
{{milestone:{label:25.11,id:UT22084-089-013-2065}}}“Noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, ran in all four directions. In whatever direction Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, went, those ten thousand fish looked piteously in that direction at Jalavāhana.
{{milestone:{label:25.12,id:UT22084-089-013-2066}}}“Noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, again ran in all four directions but did not find water, so then he looked into the four directions and saw many trees that were not very far away. He climbed those trees and cut off branches. Carrying those tree branches, he went back to the great lake, and there he created a very cool shade for those ten thousand fish.
{{milestone:{label:25.13,id:UT22084-089-013-2067}}}“Then, noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, went searching for the river that flowed into that lake. Wherever he ran in the four directions, he did not find the river that flowed into the lake. He hurriedly followed a dried-up riverbed. There was a great river called Jalāgamā, and it was the waters of that river that had flowed into that lake in the empty{{note:{index:489,id:UT22084-089-013-2068}}} wilderness.{{note:{index:490,id:UT22084-089-013-2069}}} At that time, a wicked being,{{note:{index:491,id:UT22084-089-013-2070}}} in order to obtain those ten thousand fish, had caused the river to flow into a great ravine{{note:{index:492,id:UT22084-089-013-2071}}} in that area so that subsequently there would be no water flowing to the fish. When Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, saw that, he thought, ‘Not even a thousand people could make the course of this river flow to that lake, so how would I alone be able to?’ He then returned.
{{milestone:{label:25.14,id:UT22084-089-013-2072}}}“Then, noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, hurriedly went to King Sureśvaraprabha. Having reached him, he bowed down his head to the feet of King Sureśvaraprabha, seated himself in one direction, and told his story: ‘I had eliminated illness in all the villages, towns, and market towns within Your Majesty’s domain.{{note:{index:493,id:UT22084-089-013-2073}}}{{page:{number:220,id:UT22084-089-013-3171,folio:F.261.a}}} In a certain place, there is a lake called Aṭavīsaṃbhavā, in which live ten thousand fish. They lack water and are being tormented by the sun. Just as I did for human beings, I wish to save the lives of those who have been born as animals. Therefore, Your Majesty, I request twenty elephants from you.’
{{milestone:{label:25.15,id:UT22084-089-013-2074}}}“King Sureśvaraprabha gave his ministers the command: ‘Give the great king of doctors twenty elephants!’
{{milestone:{label:25.16,id:UT22084-089-013-2075}}}“The ministers said to him, ‘Great being! Go to the elephant pen, take away twenty elephants, and bring benefit and happiness to beings!’
{{milestone:{label:25.17,id:UT22084-089-013-2076}}}“Then, noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, with his sons Jalāmbara and Jalagarbha, led away twenty elephants and obtained from the elephant keepers one hundred ox-leather bags, and then they returned, going to where great river Jalāgamā flowed. They filled those bags with water, loaded them onto the elephants, and hurried back to the lake in the empty wilderness. When they had arrived there, they took down the water from the elephants, and from all four directions they filled the lake with water. As Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, walked in the four directions, wherever he went, the ten thousand fish sped there.
{{milestone:{label:25.18,id:UT22084-089-013-2077}}}“Then, noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, wondered, ‘Why are the ten thousand fish speeding to wherever I am?’ He also thought, ‘These ten thousand fish are definitely tormented by the fire of hunger and are begging me for food, so I will give them food.’
{{milestone:{label:25.19,id:UT22084-089-013-2078}}}“Then, noble goddess, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, said to his son Jalāmbara, ‘Mount the fastest of all these elephants ride as quickly as you can to our{{note:{index:494,id:UT22084-089-013-2079}}} home, and say to your grandfather, the head merchant, “O grandfather, Jalavāhana has said, {{page:{number:221,id:UT22084-089-013-3172,folio:F.261.b}}} ‘Put together as one all the food that my parents, brothers, sisters, male servants, female servants, and workmen have at home, and send it to me quickly in the hands of Jalāmbara riding the elephant!’ ” ’
{{milestone:{label:25.20,id:UT22084-089-013-2080}}}“Then the boy Jalāmbara, riding that elephant, rode and galloped as quickly as he could and came to his home. When he had arrived there, he told his story in detail. Then the boy Jalāmbara loaded onto the elephant all that combined food that he had been told to obtain, and he rode that elephant to the lake in the empty wilderness.
{{milestone:{label:25.21,id:UT22084-089-013-2081}}}“Jalavāhana was delighted to see his son Jalāmbara, received the food from his son, divided it, and scattered it in the lake, satisfying those ten thousand fish.
{{milestone:{label:25.22,id:UT22084-089-013-2082}}}“He thought, ‘At another time, in a solitary place, I heard from a bhikṣu reading the Mahāyāna that someone who hears the name of the Tathāgata Ratnaśikhin at the time of death will be reborn in a happy existence in a higher world.{{note:{index:495,id:UT22084-089-013-2083}}} So I will teach the fish the profound Dharma of dependent origination and also recite the name of the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha Ratnaśikhin.’ 
{{milestone:{label:25.23,id:UT22084-089-013-2084}}}“At that time, the beings in Jambudvīpa had two views. Some had faith in the Mahāyāna and some disparaged it.
{{milestone:{label:25.24,id:UT22084-089-013-2085}}}“Then, at that time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, stood in the lake up to his knees and recited: ‘Homage to the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha Ratnaśikhin. Previously, when the Tathāgata Ratnaśikhin was practicing bodhisattva conduct, he made this prayer: “May anyone in the ten directions who hears my name at the time of their death, {{page:{number:222,id:UT22084-089-013-3173,folio:F.262.a}}} after their passing be reborn with the good fortune of becoming devas in Trāyastriṃśa.” ’
{{milestone:{label:25.25,id:UT22084-089-013-2086}}}“Then Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, taught this Dharma to those who had been reborn as animals: ‘Because this exists, that is produced; because this is born, that is born. In that way, because of the factor of ignorance, there is formation; because of the factor of formation, there is consciousness; because of the factor of consciousness, there is name and form; because of the factor of name and form, there are the six āyatanas; because of the factor of the six āyatanas, there is contact; because of the factor of contact, there is sensation; because of the factor of sensation, there is craving; because of the factor of craving, there is grasping; because of the factor of grasping, there is becoming; because of the factor of becoming, there is birth; because of the factor of birth, there is old age, death, misery, lamenting, suffering, unhappiness, and distress. In that way there is produced this great mass of nothing but suffering. 
{{milestone:{label:25.26,id:UT22084-089-013-2087}}}“ ‘Thus, through the cessation of ignorance, formation ceases, and so on, until in that way this great mass of nothing but suffering ceases.’
{{milestone:{label:25.27,id:UT22084-089-013-2088}}}“Noble goddess, in that way, at that time, in that time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, recited those words of the Dharma to those who had been reborn as animals. Then, together with his sons, Jalāmbara and Jalagarbha, he returned to his home.
{{milestone:{label:25.28,id:UT22084-089-013-2089}}}“At another time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, ate a great feast and became intoxicated from alcohol, and then went to sleep in his bed. At that time, in that time, there appeared a great omen. When that night had passed, it was time for the ten thousand fish to die, and they were reborn with the good fortune of becoming devas in Trāyastriṃśa. As soon as they were born there, this manner of thought arose in their minds: {{page:{number:223,id:UT22084-089-013-3174,folio:F.262.b}}} ‘Through what good karma as a cause have we been reborn among the devas of Trāyastriṃśa?’ Then they thought, ‘We were ten thousand fish in Jambudvīpa. We had been reborn as animals, but Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, satisfied us with much water and the most excellent food, and then he taught us the profound Dharma of dependent origination and recited the name of the tathāgata arhat samyaksaṃbuddha Ratnaśikhin. It is through that good quality as a cause and as a condition that we have been reborn here among the Trāyastriṃśa devas. We must go to where Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, is and, after arriving there, make offerings to him.’
{{milestone:{label:25.29,id:UT22084-089-013-2090}}}“Then those ten thousand devas vanished from among the Trāyastriṃśa devas and arrived at the home of Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son.
{{milestone:{label:25.30,id:UT22084-089-013-2091}}}“At that time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, was sleeping on his bed, and those devas placed ten thousand pearl necklaces above his head. They placed a hundred thousand pearl necklaces in front of his feet. They placed a hundred thousand pearl necklaces to his right. They placed a hundred thousand pearl necklaces to his left. They also sent down a great rain of coral tree flowers that came up to the knees. They also played divine music that woke up everyone in Jambudvīpa. Then those ten thousand devas went up into the sky and sent down a rain of coral tree flowers here and there throughout the domain of King Sureśvaraprabha. Then they went to the great lake in the empty wilderness and sent down a great rain of coral tree flowers onto that great lake. Then they vanished from there and returned to their paradise where they delighted and amused themselves with the five sensory pleasures, enjoyed pleasures, and experienced splendor and good fortune.
{{milestone:{label:25.31,id:UT22084-089-013-2092}}}“In Jambudvīpa, at dawn, King Sureśvaraprabha saw that these signs had occurred, and he asked his astrologers and prime ministers, {{page:{number:224,id:UT22084-089-013-3175,folio:F.263.a}}} ‘Why did these signs appear last night?’
{{milestone:{label:25.32,id:UT22084-089-013-2093}}}“They answered, ‘Your Majesty should know this: a rain of forty thousand pearl necklaces and also a rain of divine coral tree flowers fell in the home of Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son.’ 
{{milestone:{label:25.33,id:UT22084-089-013-2094}}}“King Sureśvaraprabha said to his ministers, ‘You go and summon Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, with pleasant words.’ 
{{milestone:{label:25.34,id:UT22084-089-013-2095}}}“Then the astrologers and prime ministers went to the home of Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, and having arrived they said to Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, ‘King Sureśvaraprabha is summoning you.’
{{milestone:{label:25.35,id:UT22084-089-013-2096}}}“Then Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, went with the prime ministers to King Sureśvaraprabha.
{{milestone:{label:25.36,id:UT22084-089-013-2097}}}“King Sureśvaraprabha said to him, ‘Jalavāhana, such kinds of signs appeared last night. Do you know why there were those signs?’
{{milestone:{label:25.37,id:UT22084-089-013-2098}}}“Then, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, said to King Sureśvaraprabha, ‘Your Majesty, I know that the time of death definitely came for those ten thousand fish.’
{{milestone:{label:25.38,id:UT22084-089-013-2099}}}“The king asked, ‘How do you know that, Jalavāhana?’
{{milestone:{label:25.39,id:UT22084-089-013-2100}}}“ ‘Your Majesty,’ said Jalavāhana. ‘I will send Jalāmbara to that lake to see whether those ten thousand fish are dead or alive.’
{{milestone:{label:25.40,id:UT22084-089-013-2101}}}“ ‘Do that!’ commanded the king.
{{milestone:{label:25.41,id:UT22084-089-013-2102}}}“Then Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, said to his son Jalāmbara, ‘Son, go to see whether the ten thousand fish in the lake in the empty wilderness have died or not.’
{{milestone:{label:25.42,id:UT22084-089-013-2103}}}“Then the son, Jalāmbara, went as quickly as he could to that great lake in the empty wilderness and saw that the time of death had come for those ten thousand fish and that a great rain of coral tree flowers had fallen there. He returned and said to his father, ‘Their time of death had come.’
{{milestone:{label:25.43,id:UT22084-089-013-2104}}}“Then Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, having heard those words, went to King Sureśvaraprabha and told him in detail what had occurred: ‘The time of death had come to all those ten thousand fish, and they were reborn among the devas of Trāyastriṃśa. It is through their and my{{note:{index:496,id:UT22084-089-013-2105}}} power that those good signs appeared last night. {{page:{number:225,id:UT22084-089-013-3176,folio:F.263.b}}} There also fell a rain of forty thousand strings of pearls and divine coral tree flowers in my home.’
{{milestone:{label:25.44,id:UT22084-089-013-2106}}}“Then the king was happy, pleased, and overjoyed.”
{{milestone:{label:25.45,id:UT22084-089-013-2107}}}The Bhagavat then said to the goddess Bodhisattvasamuccayā, “Noble goddess, do not hold the view of thinking that at that time, in that time, King Sureśvaraprabha was anyone else. Why is that? It is because during that time the Śākya Daṇḍapāṇi was King Sureśvaraprabha.
{{milestone:{label:25.46,id:UT22084-089-013-2108}}}“Noble goddess, do not hold the view of thinking that at that time, in that time, the head merchant Jaṭiṃdhara was anyone else. Why is that? It is because during that time King Śuddhodana was the head merchant Jaṭiṃdhara. 
{{milestone:{label:25.47,id:UT22084-089-013-2109}}}“Noble goddess, do not hold the view of thinking that at that time, in that time, Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son, was anyone else. Why is that? It is because during that time I was Jalavāhana, the head merchant’s son.
{{milestone:{label:25.48,id:UT22084-089-013-2110}}}“Noble goddess, do not hold the view of thinking that at that time, in that time, his wife, Jalāmbujagarbhā, was anyone else. Why is that? It is because during that time the Śākya maiden Gopā was his wife, Jalāmbujagarbhā.
